Current Commentary

Financial Emergency and the Responsibility of the Chinese People 14

Our city has seen a large outflow of silver in recent days. It is estimated that nearly eight million yuan has been exported. As a result, the money market is extremely tight. The market has suddenly shown signs of panic, and society is also feeling uneasy. In recent days, the municipal government has discussed, the silver firms have consulted, and the financial community has held meetings. All believe that the turmoil in Tianjin has caused public unrest. Many citizens are storing cash, and foreign banks are also absorbing a large amount of silver dollars. Therefore, the biggest reason for the financial emergency is the impact of the current situation. If this inference is indeed true, then we must recognize that the Chinese people have not yet fully understood the nation's crisis and their own responsibility to the country. In other words, they have not yet fully realized how closely and inseparably they are related to the nation.

The nation is currently plagued by internal floods and threatened by external enemies. The chance of survival hangs by a thread. This is precisely the time when responsible citizens, those with strength, should contribute their strength, and those with wealth should contribute their wealth to overcome the national crisis together. At this time, only the interests of the nation and the interests of the people matter. Individuals should embrace the spirit of absolute sacrifice to overcome the national crisis. Only by overcoming the national crisis can individual difficulties be resolved, and only by safeguarding the interests of the nation can individual interests be obtained. For a nation is like a boat carrying its people; if the boat sinks, all aboard will drown. If the nation perishes, all its people will become slaves. This principle is clear. To take a step back, society is a whole organization, and all social strata are inextricably linked. The prosperity or decline of one part directly or indirectly affects the prosperity or decline of the entire society. Therefore, merely seeking one's own well-being while ignoring the suffering of the entire society is also unacceptable to reality.

Today, due to the tense situation, people are rushing to withdraw and store cash, and many are storing large amounts of cash in foreign banks. We infer that their psychology is, "If I can deposit money in a foreign bank, even if there is prolonged turmoil in the country, I will not suffer any panic," or "Even if the country is destroyed and the nation is enslaved, I can still be a wealthy person living under someone else's roof." Alas, this very thought is enough to destroy our country and enslave our people. If anyone holds this thought, they must admit that their heart is dead, their blood is frozen, and their vitality is exhausted. They must also admit that they are willing to be slaves of a fallen nation without regret.

The financial emergency will inevitably cause panic in our market to expand day by day. Moreover, the panic in the market will inevitably affect the economic boycott movement against Japan. Therefore, this is not only due to the impact of the current situation, but also to the conspiracy of the Japanese to disrupt our market and undermine our economic boycott movement. We should be keenly aware of this conspiracy and prevent its realization. The only weapon is the patriotic fervor in every Chinese person.

With the national crisis at hand, overcoming the crisis is the responsibility of the Chinese people. Each of us is a cell of the nation, and the nation is where each of us is rooted. There is an individual only after there is a nation. When the skin survives, the hair attaches to it. The lives of the people of a fallen nation are in the hands of others. What more is there to say about external wealth? Looking at the world, there is no shortage of precedents. This is something the Chinese people must realize first.

With the national crisis pressing, the market must not be allowed to be disrupted in any way. Even minor things, such as the arrival of winter, must not be allowed to inflict this blow on the market, causing it to be even more bleak and increasing the risk of winter disasters. Therefore, the Chinese people should all pay attention to this issue and, in particular, display patriotic fervor to prevent this crisis. From now on, if anyone abandons himself to the Chinese people and stores large amounts of cash in foreign banks, it would be no different from Yuan Jinkai and Xi Qia's open betrayal of the country. Our financial community should monitor them closely, and the entire nation should rise up and impose effective sanctions on them.

Japanese Withdrawal of Troops Attacking Jinzhou 15

The reason for Japan's sudden withdrawal of troops attacking Jinzhou this time is no more than two points. One is that Japan knows that the Chinese side will not agree to the resolution of the League of Nations without withdrawing its troops. Therefore, it first made a big show of attacking Jinzhou, increasing military pressure and threatening our people to cause extreme panic. Then, it retreated and stopped the attack on Jinzhou to appease the Chinese people and give the appearance of complying with China's demand for troop withdrawal, so that China could use this as a way to step down and accept the resolution of the League of Nations' investigation team. This is a strategy to deceive China. The other is that the League of Nations has recently been eager to achieve its resolution and prevent its mask of peace from being broken. It is doing its best to persuade China to accept it. If Japan continues its attack on Jinzhou, it will inevitably make it more difficult for China to agree, and the opportunity to accept it will be further away. Therefore, the United States, Britain, and France have unanimously tried to stop Japan's attack on Jinzhou. Japan is afraid that holding on too firmly will provoke a backlash from the major powers. Under this mutual understanding, it is accommodating the League of Nations' opinion. This is another strategy to appease the League of Nations.

Japan's intention today is focused on winning the victory of the League of Nations' resolution, striving to occupy a sufficient foothold for activities in the resolution. On troop withdrawal, it insists on not setting a deadline. On investigation, it does not allow interference with its military operations. In the neutral zone, it insists on retaining Japanese residents, and if they encounter danger, the Japanese army can still enter. If these conditions are met, then not only will direct negotiations be able to go smoothly in everything in the future, but military action can also be carried out freely at any time. If it wants to attack Jinzhou, then attacking Jinzhou will have nothing to restrain it. Why rush today? Therefore, Japan must strive to achieve this new resolution quickly. To achieve it quickly, it may as well use the withdrawal of troops attacking Jinzhou as a strategy of seeming to release in order to capture. On the one hand, it is doing its best to harass in Tianjin, expanding the military scope of the Northeast to the military scope of North China, in order to increase the pressure of future direct negotiations. The Japanese are so cunning, and are there still Chinese people who are pleased with Japan's troop withdrawal?

Domestic Important Telegrams Two

League of Nations Drafting Committee 16

Continued Meeting Yesterday

Resolution Expected to Pass on Wednesday

Shi Zhaoji Still Insists on Deadline for Troop Withdrawal

Both Chinese and Japanese Replies Have Been Sent to the League of Nations

Paris, although today is Sunday, the drafting committee of the League of Nations Council held a meeting at the French Foreign Ministry at 11:30 this morning. Japanese representative Ito delivered Japan's reply to the League of Nations resolution. It is heard that the content includes several proposed preventive amendments. Although Japan agrees to instruct the commander-in-chief to prohibit troops from advancing and hostile actions, it must be stipulated that if the Japanese army is attacked by bandits, it will fight back. Today, Chinese representative Shi sent a letter to Briand, informing him that China agrees to the Council's proposal to establish a neutral zone near Jinzhou. The Chinese representative received an official report stating that the Chinese government has instructed the military commander of Jinzhou to enter into an agreement with the foreign military observers there, etc. In addition, the British military observer in Qiqihar reported to the Council that the city is completely under the control of Japanese soldiers. Although there was no major chaos when the Japanese army entered the city, no Chinese personnel have been handling affairs to date. Most Japanese residents have returned, and the Japanese army does not appear to be advancing north. It is said that airplanes were sent to the northeast for reconnaissance the next day. (29th National Telegram)

Paris, this morning, the League of Nations heard the news that an unexpected diplomatic incident between the United States and Japan has been resolved satisfactorily, which was greatly gratifying. This afternoon, the Council will still hold a secret meeting, and notices have been issued. Chinese and Japanese representatives will not attend, but Japanese representative Yoshizawa went to the drafting committee today to report Japan's attitude toward the establishment of a neutral zone in Jinzhou. It is heard that the Japanese government generally expressed its approval. Yoshizawa also denied to the committee all reports that the Japanese army was advancing toward Jinzhou and denied that Japanese aircraft had dropped bombs there. He also announced that most of the Japanese army had withdrawn from Qiqihar. US Ambassador Dawes notified Briand today that the US Army Attaché in Japan is currently in the three northeastern provinces and has received instructions to cooperate closely with other neutral observers staying in Jinzhou. (29th National Telegram)

Paris, since Japan has promised not to attack Jinzhou, the League of Nations Administrative Council is expected to agree on its proposal on Wednesday. This morning, the Administrative Council listened to Dr. Shi's opinion on this proposal. Shi still insisted that the Japanese army withdraw completely by a deadline and suggested that a period be stipulated without specifying a date. This suggestion was not supported by the members. The Administrative Council agreed to add a clause stipulating that when the investigation team arrives in Manchuria, it must report to the Administrative Council how far the Japanese army has withdrawn and whether China's plan to protect Japanese residents can be considered satisfactory. It is heard that the Administrative Council has temporarily passed this proposal this afternoon and is considering expanding the number of the investigation team. Someone proposed that the neutral observers in Jinzhou should be part of the investigation team. It is heard that the Administrative Council has rejected this, believing that the observers should cooperate with each other, exchange information, and report to their respective governments, and the governments will then forward the reports to the League of Nations. This approach seems to be more beneficial. Tomorrow morning, the drafting committee will meet with Yoshizawa to discuss the revisions. The Administrative Council will meet again in the afternoon, but Chinese and Japanese representatives will still not attend. Today, the British delegation submitted to the League of Nations Secretariat the British report on the recent events in Tianjin, stating that gunfire occurred in Tianjin on the evening of November 26, intermittently throughout the night, and stopped only in the morning. The Chinese side said that plainclothes teams attacked the Chinese police again, but the Japanese said that Chinese soldiers deliberately attacked the Japanese concession. The Japanese army used machine guns and light artillery. On the morning of November 27, several Japanese aircraft flew over Jinzhou. British observers saw that trenches had been dug in the strategic areas of Hushan on the Beining Railway line, but it was expected that the Chinese soldiers would not resist

Page 6

the Japanese army's attack. (28th Reuters Telegram)

Paris, the Chinese government's reply to the telegram from the Chairman of the Administrative Council on November 26 has been sent by representative Shi. The text is as follows: The Chinese government suggests that countries that can send observers to the vicinity of Jinzhou should issue the following instructions to the observers: (1) The observers should jointly study and delineate a neutral zone between the Chinese and Japanese armies or other systems that can avoid contact between the two armies. (2) The observers should jointly agree on a method to contact the commanders of the Chinese and Japanese armies in order to implement necessary measures. In order for these instructions to have beneficial results, the commander of the Chinese army will contact the observers. The Chinese government deeply thanks the Chairman of the Administrative Council and all members and immediately instructs the commander of the Chinese army in Jinzhou to take necessary measures with the observers to avoid contact between the Chinese and Japanese armies. (29th Havas Telegram)

Stimson's Statement 17

Did Not Make Derogatory Remarks About Japan

Re-Publication of Previous Remarks

Japanese Side's Resentment Dissipated

League of Nations Investigates the Truth in Detail

Washington, Secretary of State Stimson stated when meeting with reporters today that the Japanese Foreign Ministry's opposition to comments not made by him was a misunderstanding. Stimson then gave the verbatim record of his conversation yesterday to the newspapers and stated that he was willing to take responsibility for his words. He said, "On November 23, I instructed the ambassador to Japan to inform Japanese Foreign Minister Shidehara that I was very worried about the reports that the Japanese army commander was now planning to attack Chinese soldiers near Jinzhou. I sincerely hope that the reports are unfounded." The next day, the Japanese ambassador conveyed Shidehara's words, saying that he and the Army Minister and Chief of Staff had all agreed not to take hostile actions against Jinzhou and had issued military orders to that effect. "Looking at this reply, I cannot understand the news of Honjo's troops advancing in the reports," he said. Senator Swanson of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee met with the Secretary of State today and requested the publication of various documents issued by the United States regarding the Manchurian Incident. (28th Reuters Telegram)

Tokyo, Japanese Ambassador to the United States Debuchi visited Stimson and Cassell on the morning of the 28th upon instructions from the Japanese government to inquire whether Mr. Shi had made the statements reported in the newspapers. (29th Japanese United News Agency Telegram)

Washington, the US State Department issued a statement today regarding the Japanese Foreign Ministry's accusation against US Secretary of State Stimson, stating that Mr. Shi had not made any remarks unfavorable to Japan. The US State Department also denied that Mr. Shi had stated that Japan had ambitions to seize all of Manchuria and that the Japanese army was acting like madmen in Manchuria. In short, the US Secretary of State had not made any critical remarks about the Japanese authorities. In Tokyo, the remarks were

made by a news agency that has a cooperation agreement with it. Therefore, the US partner agency is suspected of transmitting the remarks. However, in New York, officials of the partner agency stated that there were no such remarks circulating in the country or abroad. It has been found that reports on Stimson's remarks by news agencies in the United States are slightly different, but generally the same. The two major US news agencies, the United Press and the Associated Press, both believe that Stimson's clarification of the news transmitted by the Japanese United News Agency is indeed accurate. Stimson has now ordered the publication of his conversation with reporters last Friday, the original text of which is roughly the same as that transmitted by the Associated Press and the United Press. On that day, Stimson only told reporters that he had just received a telegram that the Japanese army was approaching Jinzhou, which was very surprising. Mr. Shi also said that on November 24, Japanese Foreign Minister Shidehara had firmly stated that Japan would not attack Jinzhou. This statement was conveyed by US Ambassador to Japan Forbes. On Friday, Mr. Shi told reporters again that various countries were planning to send military attachés to Jinzhou, and the US military attaché from the US Embassy in Peiping, Magruder, was already in Jinzhou. At that time, there was no plan to establish a neutral zone around Jinzhou with Western troops, so the US State Department was unwilling to express anything about the establishment of the neutral zone or whether the United States would participate. (28th National Telegram)

Tokyo, the temporary resentment in Japan against US Secretary of State Stimson's conversation with reporters has now dissipated. Official news from Washington denied that the US Secretary of State had made any remarks criticizing Japan, and public opinion has calmed down. It is said that false rumors caused misunderstandings, and both sides expressed regret. Although some people are worried that China's attitude toward Japan may become tougher due to these unfounded rumors, the misunderstanding has now ended, so the Foreign Ministry will not issue any statements in response to the falsely reported accusations made by Stimson. (29th Reuters Telegram) Paris, today, the League of Nations Council and people in the League of Nations are paying close attention to the unexpected attack incident between US Secretary of State Stimson and Japanese Foreign Minister Shidehara. Although the League of Nations Secretariat has no official relationship, it has ordered a detailed investigation of the facts. League of Nations officials are keeping silent in accordance with diplomatic etiquette, but they said that Tokyo's reaction was too emotional and easily aroused criticism. However, this matter has a tendency to consolidate the position of the Council, because it shows that the US position is the same as the League of Nations' attitude. (29th National Society Telegram)

Bandits Discovered in Luandong

Driven by the Japanese

Plotting to Disrupt Transportation

Tuantai Mountain, Shimenqian, Anshan, east of Luan County, Beiping, on the night of the 28th, discovered about 100 plainclothes troops and bandits driven by the Japanese, plotting to disrupt transportation. The local garrison heard the news and rushed to suppress them, and assisted the railway police in protecting various trains. Fortunately, there was no riot. (29th Special Telegram)

Qinhuangdao 18

Two Japanese Warships Arrived Yesterday

Tianjin, at 6:00 am on the 29th, two Japanese warships arrived in Qinhuangdao. At 7:00 am, one US warship arrived. (29th Special)

Panic Among Merchants and Residents in Beiping City

Repairing Iron Plate and Wooden Railings

Beiping City merchants and residents, seeing the devastation in Tianjin, have become wary. Therefore, merchants in various key locations, in addition to piling up a large number of sandbags, have also raised huge sums of money to repair thick iron plate and wooden railings. Yesterday, the shops in Qianmen Avenue, Langfang Second Street, Xianyu Kou, Zhenbao City, etc., were all working day and night to rush the construction. (29th Special Telegram)

The Beiping Public Security Bureau sent police to advise the merchants to operate with peace of mind and not to alarm each other. (29th Special Telegram)

The Hebei Provincial Government of Beiping consulted the Municipal Government, informing the farmers in the four rural areas to strictly prohibit the wholesale of large quantities of grain and millet to the Japanese. (29th Special Telegram)

Bao Wenyue Discusses Diplomacy 19

Bao Wenyue arrived in Beiping this afternoon and talked about the central government's diplomacy toward Japan, still based on the original policy. After Gu Weijun becomes the Minister of Foreign Affairs, the diplomatic situation will definitely have new developments. In short, our country will never yield. Chiang Kai-shek's Telegram to Wang Jingwei 21

Urging Comrades in Guangdong to Enter the Capital as Soon as Possible

Nanjing, Chiang Kai-shek sent a telegram to Wang Jingwei, and telegraphed the text to Cai, Zhang, Li, and other members, also to urge their departure. The two telegrams are recorded below:

(1) Telegram to Wang Jingwei: To Mr. Wang Jingwei and all comrades in Guangdong, greetings. This time, public opinion throughout the country believes that only the unity of our party can save the country from the national crisis. It is not that the people are disgusted with our party, but rather that they believe that if our party is still divided, the national crisis will be even more unimaginable. Zhongzheng is apprehensive, so he specially sent Mr. Cai, Zhang, and Chen to Guangdong to present this idea. Fortunately, Mr. Wang and others shared this fear and agreed to come to Shanghai to form a united front. Zhongzheng also contributed his difficult views on unity at the Fourth Plenary Session. Fortunately, the comrades at the conference worked together to live up to the expectations of the people. All endured the pain and tears and resolutely compromised on the newly elected law and quickly completed the conference affairs. It has been more than a week since the adjournment of the conference. All this is to speed up the process of resisting the disaster through unity and dare not delay the days and mislead the party and the country. After the adjournment of the conference, I eagerly hope that the comrades in Guangdong will come to the capital within the month as agreed to immediately achieve the great benefit of collective wisdom. Then, in the face of a major disaster, compared with the ordinary support of the central government, there must be improvement. This is especially the unanimous public opinion today. But recently, I heard that the comrades in Guangdong have been meeting for half a month, and their opinions are still different, making unity impossible to achieve soon. This month is coming to an end, and time is running out. If there is no national crisis other than unity, then consideration can be cautious and delay will not be a big problem. But the Kou disaster is deepening and intensifying. The collective thinking of unity has not been gathered, and the credibility of the central government is falling. Mr. Wang and his comrades must deeply understand that the ordinary strategies are not suitable for joint measures. Then the old prescription will be shelved and the new agent will be delayed in dispensing. Like a critical illness, how can it be tolerated? Zhongzheng is rushing north to wait for the full meeting to open, so that he can be ordered to set out with a follow. Otherwise, the central plan will not be allowed to be informed by Zhongzheng before departure. If at that time there are still a few who cannot avoid the differences in Guangdong today, temporarily delaying the situation of mutual restraint, even if it is easy to correct, and the advancement has this concern of looking back, it is easy to fall into a situation where advancement and retreat are impossible. Then, the success or failure of the individual is not enough to care about, and misleading the country is a great crime. Therefore, I deeply hope that all comrades will be aware of the warning of fratricide and follow the purpose of resisting foreign insults, acting quickly to achieve the effect of unity through immediate assembly and rescue. The overall plan is decided by the central executive and supervisory plenary meeting. Mr. Wang is mediating the crisis, and I hope that he can invite nearby comrades to guide him as soon as possible. I hope even more that the comrades in Guangdong can tell me as soon as possible when they can arrive in Beijing so that the central plenary meeting can be held on time. I am waiting for your reply. Younger brother Chiang Kai-shek bows

(2) Telegram to Cai, Zhang, Li, etc.: To Mr. Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, Zhang Puquan, Wu Tiecheng, and Chen Zhenru, greetings. The telegram I sent to Jingwei earlier said, (see the previous omission), etc. I hope that you will earnestly urge the departure and come together as soon as possible. I am waiting expectantly. Zhongzheng bows, (29th Special Telegram)

Ministry of Finance Orders All Customs 25

To Prohibit the Export of Silver

According to Nanjing financial circles, the Japanese are using various methods in the Tianjin area to undermine finances and are collecting silver dollars in Shanghai to transport to Dalian. Their intention is to reduce the amount of cash in circulation in our country and shake the silver market. Shanghai silver houses believe that the market needs a lot of cash because the accounting period for merchants is approaching. They ask to prevent the outflow as soon as possible, and in addition to taking measures to check it themselves, they also ask the Ministry of Finance to notify all customs to prohibit the export of silver. It is reported that the Ministry of Finance will implement this in the near future. In addition, due to the lack of cash in the markets of Hankou and Jinan, the provincial and municipal authorities have announced a ban on the export of silver dollars and large remittances and have submitted this to the Ministry of Finance for record. (29th Dispatch)

International Disarmament Conference 51

To be Convened in Geneva Next February

Delegates from Various Countries Sing the Praises of Peace

But are Greatly Insulted in Paris

The National News Agency, Geneva, 26th: The Secretariat of the League of Nations recently stated that the rumors that the Disarmament Conference will be postponed are completely unfounded. The Secretariat stated that no country has requested the postponement of the Disarmament Conference so far, nor has this issue been raised in any way. Preparations for the conference are proceeding with great effort, and the Swiss postal authorities have also made special arrangements for this matter to facilitate direct communication between the various delegations and governments and to provide special convenience for journalists. It is expected that hundreds of journalists will gather here at that time. At the same time, regarding the issue of disarmament, France has expressed difficulties regarding the prospects for disarmament, insisting that it is unwilling to reduce its armaments slightly without sufficient guarantees. Recently, the International Disarmament Discussion Meeting was held in Paris, and the British representative, Seir Cecil and others, were surrounded by anti-disarmament rioters, who insulted and scolded them. Seir Cecil and others are all people of great renown who advocate international peace, but now they have been insulted by rioters in a foreign capital. Therefore, many German newspapers have criticized this, saying, "If a Frenchman went to Berlin to promote peace and friendship and was subjected to such insults, would the French newspapers remain silent?" It is also reported that the five people who were arrested at the meeting due to the riots have now been released, which is also enough to leave an unpleasant impression.

Japan Plans to Increase Taxes and Borrow Money 52

To Fill the Revenue Shortfall

The Electric News Agency, Tokyo, 29th: The Ministry of Finance decided yesterday afternoon to issue a huge amount of public bonds and increase tax rates to fill the shortfall in the next year's revenue budget. The Minister of Finance will first consult with the cabinet tomorrow, and then discuss with the party executives. The final decision will be made at the cabinet meeting on December 4th. (1) "Form of Public Bond Issuance": In addition to the original telephone bonds and post-earthquake reconstruction bonds, the public bonds used to supplement revenue and the unemployment bonds will be considered general accounting and will all be attributed to the public bonds used to fill revenue shortfalls. (2) "Tax Increase Rate": (A) Income Tax: (1) Comprehensive income tax will be increased by 1.5 percentage points on the current rate of 5 percent to 6.5 percent. (2) The second type of income tax will be increased by 1 percentage point on the current rate of 4 percent to 5 percent. (3) The third type of income tax will be increased by 10 percent. (B) The capital interest tax will be increased by 1.5 percentage points to 3 percent. Other inheritance taxes and gasoline taxes will remain at the current rates. (3) The total amount of tax increase is 40 million yuan, but the amount of tax increase is 5 million yuan less than the planned amount, and the amount of public bonds is more than the planned amount, namely (1) deficit bonds of 60 million yuan and (2) unemployment bonds of 45 million yuan, totaling 110 million yuan.

British-Indian Round Table Conference Plenary Session 53

Reuters, London, 28th: The final plenary session of the Indian Round Table Conference began today. The chairman, Sankey, and the British Prime Minister, MacDonald, said that in order to make the work of the conference public, they intend to formally propose to pass the reports of the Federal Structure Committee and the Minorities Committee. There are currently fifty delegates requesting to speak, so the conference will have to be extended until Tuesday to conclude. The British Prime Minister will report on the British government's policy towards India before the end. Sankey said that the Federal Structure Committee has approved the committee's report, but the representatives of Muslims and other minorities have reserved their opinions on national defense, diplomacy, finance, and commerce, and will only withdraw their reservations after the minority issues have been satisfactorily resolved.

The National News Agency, London, 28th: British Prime Minister MacDonald held the first conference of the second Indian Round Table Conference at 10:30 this morning in the Queen Anne reception hall of St. James's Palace. One hundred and five delegates were present and sat around the round table. MacDonald gave the opening speech. Meetings will continue this afternoon and evening, but Gandhi may not have the opportunity to speak until Monday. Although Monday is Gandhi's day of silence, it is said that Gandhi also intends to break the rule if it is necessary to speak for the benefit of the National Congress.

Indian Government 54

Actively Preventing Gandhi's Movement

Havas, Bombay, 28th: Gandhi's movement is about to happen again. The Indian government has begun to take preventive measures and has deployed troops at important military locations for defense. This force is assisted by tanks and aircraft and can take a strong offensive when necessary to avoid the danger of most white troops facing hostile actions in densely populated areas. The Indian government is setting up radio stations in important cities and towns along various railway lines for mutual communication because railway, telegraph, and telephone personnel may go on strike. Gandhi seems to be using opposition to taxes as an excuse to repeat the non-resistance movement. The various taxes were originally intended to be reduced separately, but due to recent financial difficulties, they have been increased instead, which has caused dissatisfaction among the people. Gandhi's request at the National Congress for a review of the rights acquired by the British on tea, mines, rubber, ships, land, and various patents has only made the British more united and formed a united front. According to the two representatives who returned from the Round Table Conference, the failure of this conference was actually due to Gandhi's excessive demands. It is also rumored that Gandhi has been suffering from a cold for several days, but he still attended the Round Table Conference today. Gandhi's condition is not worth worrying about at all, and rumors cannot be believed.

Lanzhou to all newspaper offices, formerly Gansu Province had differences between military and civilian chiefs, resulting in disputes. After further discussion, it was agreed that Ma Hongbin would lead the 7th Division back to Ningxia, and Lei Zhongtian's troops would be stationed in Lanzhou to handle the aftermath, and everything would be referred to the Central Government. All the people of Gansu are grateful for the mediation of General Wu and the Chairman of Qinghai and should respectfully report it by telegram. They also urge the Central Government to quickly decide on the aftermath of Gansu Province for easy compliance. Furthermore, the Japanese寇 are invading the east, and the nation is about to perish. Patriots are planning peaceful unification and jointly resisting foreign insults, and the generals of Qinghai, Ningxia, Sichuan, and Gansu provinces are sending joint telegrams to request General Wu to come out of the mountains to preside over foreign military affairs. It is believed that General Wu is an old statesman who, although retired in Sichuan for many years, has a heart of patriotism and concern for the people. As evidenced by the mediation of the Gansu situation, it is clear that Lian Po is still heroic and capable of killing thieves despite his age. If he rises again in Jinghan, he will be able to defend the country. People with the duty of everyone to protect the country, dare to express sincerity and be willing to be ghosts after death, rather than slaves in life. The Central Government and the people of the whole country are asked to unite and urge, so as to initiate the people's spirit and build the purpose of saving the country. At the time of the telegram, we are saddened and respectfully report our heartfelt words. We ask for your attention and await your instruction. Gansu gentry, merchants, and academic circles Yang Sijie, Shi Hou, Pei Jianzhun, Li Keming, Zheng Jun, Deng Longmu, Chouqi, Ma Zhaowu, Feng Wanglian, Zhang Jian, Liao Yuanji, Wang Wu, Qi Yin Jia, Zhang Binlun, Guo 忐, Jing Shui枬, Chen Qinshi, Wang Weiping, Yang Tingzhen, Guo Hanru, Wang Po Hou, Deng Chungao, etc. bow.

Important News

Japanese Troops Again Distort Tianjin 59

First, Plainclothes Troops are Sent to Cause Disturbances

Then Japanese Troops Immediately Fire Artillery into the Chinese Territory

Tianjin Correspondence: Since the Chinese and Japanese authorities agreed to withdraw defenses, in order to maintain the security of Tianjin and the lives and property of merchants of all countries, we have compromised and resolutely withdrawn defenses first. However, the Japanese concession authorities have made various excuses to deliberately delay until now, and have failed to remove defensive works as agreed. On the contrary, they have secretly stepped up military deployments, a large number of marines have entered Tianjin from Tanggu in disguise, and they continue to recruit plainclothes troops and hide them in the Haiguang Temple barracks, attempting to revive. Recently, it was heard that two ships of ammunition were secretly transported to Tianjin from Tanggu by hired civilian ships. Hara, the mastermind of the last incident, has also sneaked into Tianjin again. Therefore, rumors have been spreading in the city in recent days, and people are panicked. Yesterday afternoon, the situation became more and more serious, and disturbances by plainclothes thugs occurred again at night. Although the number of thugs was not as large as last time, the Japanese troops fired artillery like a string of beads, which was even more serious than on the evening of the 8th. The initial gunfire was at 8:14, and half an hour later, the entire city heard artillery fire, which became denser after 10:00. It subsided slightly around 12:00 for a short time, and then started again after 1:00 this morning. The artillery fire continued until about 3:00. The plainclothes troops were divided into two groups. One group of about twenty or thirty people was first discovered in Potaizhuang and was quickly repulsed. The other group, it was heard, had more than a hundred people and wanted to attack the Public Security Bureau from the Zhakou direction, but was also repulsed. First, gunfire was discovered in Xiguangkai at 8:14. At 8:15, it was identified that there were thirty or forty plainclothes troops south of Huaiqingli, firing guns at our side. At 8:20, an artillery shell suddenly fired from the Japanese barracks, with a loud bang, shocking the entire city. At 8:24, twenty or thirty plainclothes troops were discovered again in the Xiaotili area of Potaizhuang near Haiguang Temple in the Sixth District of the Second District, firing at our police on duty. Our security team rushed to the scene and retaliated with hand-held grenades to prevent bullets from falling into the concession. At that time, the louder sound than the gunfire was hand-held grenades, not artillery shells. Section Chief Shen of the Municipal Government immediately notified the Japanese consul of the discovery of plainclothes troops everywhere. At 9:14, the Japanese concession's electricity was completely cut off, and the French and Italian concessions also temporarily imposed martial law, prohibiting pedestrians from traveling, and dispatched armed police and police officers. At 9:26, bullets suddenly fired from the roof of the Zhongyuan Company, firing at the Chinese territory. At 9:49, Japanese troops used machine guns and artillery to fiercely attack the Chinese territory from the Zhakou direction, shaking off a window of the Telephone Bureau. The wall of the exchange room of the Telephone Bureau was destroyed by artillery shells, and the machine was also damaged, but the workers did not leave the bureau. The back wall of the 15th squadron of the South Xiejie Security Team was also destroyed by artillery fire. An artillery shell landed on Dongmalu, killing three policemen. Another three artillery shells landed behind the wall of the Provincial Government. At 10:24, the Japanese troops in the Zhakou area fired dozens of small steel cannons at the Chinese territory. At the same time, Haiguang Temple also fired guns and artillery shells, landing more than ten on Dongmalu and more than ten on Ningjia Bridge, wounding one of our policemen. Three artillery shells landed near the Jinjiayao power plant in the Fifth District of the First District, two artillery shells landed at the Fourth District Public Office on Dajing Road, and one artillery shell landed at the Provincial Government. At 2:30 this morning, the artillery fire sounded again, followed by gunfire, and the situation was very serious. Until 3:30, the Japanese troops' artillery and guns attacked the Chinese territory every few minutes. After receiving the news, the municipal and provincial authorities immediately convened a meeting to discuss measures and telegraphed the deputy commander's office in Beiping to request instructions.

The Sixth District of the Second District was taken over by our side by Section Chief Ge Jiaqi of the Fifth District of the First District, in coordination with Section Chief Pan Enrong of the Sixth District of the Second District. After negotiations with Captain Matsushita, the area commander of the Japanese troops in Haiguang Temple, it was returned. However, all documents and seals were gone. Therefore, the takeover of the Sixth District of the Second District was only an empty building. The items inside the building were empty, and local police affairs could not be carried out. Although it is called a takeover, it is actually still occupied by Japanese troops. Yesterday afternoon, the reporter went to the area of the Sixth District of the Second District to inspect. Passing the west entrance of Luan Street, the defensive line set up by the Japanese was still there. In front was a barbed wire fence, and behind it were several layers of earthworks. The Japanese flag was flying in the wind, and three or four Japanese soldiers were patrolling with guns. The situation was no different from before the takeover. I saw a hole through which people could pass, but they had to be inspected by the Japanese troops before they could pass. In the Sixth District of the Second District, only Inspector Xing led six or seven policemen stationed inside the station, and there were two doormen outside. There were no Chinese police on the street. Thirty or forty Japanese soldiers who withdrew from the Sixth District of the Second District the day before forcibly occupied civilian houses about three feet north of the station. The entire street was completely under the influence of the Japanese police. In general, the Japanese side's defensive lines were not removed everywhere, and it was clear that there were other conspiracies. Another serious incident occurred last night, which shows that the Japanese troops in the Sixth District of the Second District insisted on not returning it, which was actually kept as a base for hiding plainclothes troops. (27th)

Zhang Jinghui Does Not Go to Heilongjiang 60

Harbin Already Within Japanese Sphere of Influence

Ma Zhanshan Stationed in Hailun Reorganizing Troops

Harbin Dispatch: Zhang Jinghui's trip to Heilongjiang has been called off. Today, Zhang told Mu Weitang, representative of the Harbin General Chamber of Commerce, and Zhang Xiangting, president of the Binjiang Municipal Chamber of Commerce, who came to visit, that "My initial intention was to go to Heilongjiang to seek a relief strategy due to Chairman Ma Zhanshan's military actions against the Japanese army and the dangerous situation. Now that the matter has passed and mediation is impossible, I have abandoned the idea of going to Heilongjiang. The rumors outside about my intentions or secret trip to Heilongjiang are all speculation. As for Harbin, it is located in the center of the Northeast and is extremely important. The Japanese army may not necessarily want to come here. In order to maintain the security of Harbin, I have to take precautions to prevent the Japanese army from coming and avoid unexpected events for the local area. In recent days, I have repeatedly negotiated with the Japanese Consul in Harbin, showing my intention to maintain local security and being responsible for protecting the lives and property of Japanese residents, requesting the Japanese army not to mobilize to Harbin. At that time, the Japanese Consul immediately telegraphed the military authorities of his country, and they replied satisfactorily to my proposal, saying that since Harbin does not take hostile actions against Japan, the Japanese army will definitely not mobilize to Harbin. The rumors outside that the Japanese army will come to Harbin on the 25th are purely rumors." According to the current situation in Harbin, it is still relatively stable, but according to general speculation, even if the Japanese army does not send a large team to Harbin, it will definitely increase the number of police and military police at the consulate or force the reorganization of various agencies and send Japanese advisors to monitor them separately. Although Harbin is not hostile to the Japanese army, the Japanese side may not be able to tolerate the existence of the old system of various agencies, because the Japanese Consulate is now acting as the owner and interfering in everything. What is most disappointing here are the general White Russian newspapers. When the Fang Shen Incident occurred, the White Russian newspapers all published news favorable to the Japanese side, and the Japanese Consulate also fully supplied materials. After the fall of Heihe, the attitude of the Japanese Consulate changed drastically, changing its usual gentleness to a fierce demeanor. Recently, it was reported that all Russian reporters were summoned, and Consul Tadakazu Oohashi gave them a lecture, warning that future news reports must be approved by the consulate and first be checked. All the Russian reporters were very frustrated by this lesson. After receiving this news, the general White Russians, who intended to use Japanese power to incite chaos, knew that tigers and wolves could not be co-operated, and their plan to conquer Northern Manchuria was shelved. Since Zhang Jinghui stopped going to Heilongjiang, the Japanese side used the lower-class officials and gentry of Heihe to organize an autonomous maintenance association, led by Zhao Zhongren, the former Daoyin of Hulunbuir and current provincial committee member, Li Yintang, the former Speaker of the Provincial Assembly and current provincial committee member, and Liu Dequan, the chief of police of Heilongjiang Province. They have decided to work in the former Provincial Assembly on the 25th. Zhao has been plotting the Heihe government for many years and can now take charge of everything. In Heihe, the Japanese army started to set up checkpoints on all streets on the 23rd to check pedestrians. Those who responded slightly slower were lightly beaten and humiliated, forced to kneel in the street, and severely shot to death. They also ordered the Chamber of Commerce to guide the Japanese army to check household registrations. Every time they entered a household, they arbitrarily teased women. If they found military agency name cards, they would arrest the head of the household and take him away. Many people have been arrested for this reason in recent days. Due to the oppression of the Japanese army, all shops opened completely on the 24th, but the shop assistants sat listlessly behind the counters with sad faces, without a single customer all day long. On the evening of the 23rd, a traveler, Mr. Jia, took the Qiong-Ang Road train to the Ang'angxi Station of the East Railway. The train was checked by the Japanese army, and a military uniform was found in his luggage. He was accused of being a soldier, and without explanation, he was stabbed to death with bayonets. The general passengers were shocked, but fearing the barbarity of the Japanese soldiers, no one dared to intercede for him. At present, all the valuables in the residences of important people in Heihe have been loaded and transported to South Manchuria via the Tao'ang Road. In recent days, Japanese planes have continued to scout the retreating Heilongjiang army on the Qiqihar-Koshan Road. On the 24th, they flew to Baiquan once, but due to heavy fog, they could not hover as they wished and returned. A large group of Japanese cavalry stopped at the Ningnian Station on the Qiqihar-Koshan Road, and another group stopped at the Zhongxing Town on the Bokui-Hailun Road. Because the mountains and forests ahead were continuous and the terrain was unfamiliar, they did not dare to advance. At this time, the Heilongjiang army may have a chance to reorganize. It is said that the temporary provincial government of Heilongjiang, established by Ma Zhanshan in Hailun, started working on the 24th. Because the staff of various departments have not yet arrived, it is difficult to divide the work in practice, so eight major departments, including industry, education, finance, politics, intelligence, secretarial, police, and military affairs, are temporarily established in the provincial government to carry out preliminary reorganization. In about a week, the provincial committee and the staff of various departments should arrive, and the old regulations will be restored. The troops currently retreating to Hailun include 5,000 infantry under Yuan Chonggu, 1,000 cavalry each under Cheng Zhiyuan, Wu Songshan, and Zhang Dianjiu, 2,000 infantry under Su Bingwen, and 1,000 guards and pistol teams under Ma Zhanshan. More than 2,000 militiamen from Baiquan, Qinggang, Tiebi, Mulan and other places have also arrived, and they are being supplemented and incorporated into the regular army by various brigades. Ma is also afraid that the Japanese army will attack, so he ordered the Yuan and Wu brigades to be distributed on the Suihua-Hailun section of the Huhuai Road and outside Hailun City. If the Japanese army advances further, the war will break out. Recently, many young people from various places, motivated by righteous indignation, have gone to join the army. Ma has accepted them and selected officers with excellent academic skills to train them in order to supplement the various brigades. Tonight, the soldiers of the 10th company of the 3rd battalion of the 671st regiment of the Jilin army's Xing Zhanqing brigade stationed at the Xiaohaizi Station on the Manchu line mutinied, led by the logistics officer, killing the company and platoon leaders and fleeing to Hailun to join Ma's troops. A company of the Jilin army's Su Dechen brigade stationed in Fularji also fled to join Ma's troops, which shows that the military's hearts are filled with hatred for the enemy and they are extremely dissatisfied with their commander's policy of non-resistance. Japanese Military and Police Search Extensively Inside and Outside the City

Hwangutun and Julu River Busy with Military Transport

Shenyang-Hai Road Vehicles Concentrated in Plan to Attack Jinzhou

Shenyang Dispatch: In recent days, the Japanese army has claimed that there have been many robbery cases on various streets inside and outside the city. Starting from 5:30 every night, they send many soldiers in groups to search everywhere. Any Chinese walking late at night are shot to death. There are several such cases every day. Merchants and residents inside and outside the city do not go out on the streets after 6:00 in the evening. Since last night (23rd), Japanese troops and Chinese police have been added to guard each city gate, and pedestrians entering and leaving are subjected to strict checks, and people are extremely panicked. The pseudo-agencies established in recent days, such as the finance, education, and industry bureaus and the Northeast Communications Committee, were previously guarded by Chinese police. Recently, Japanese troops have been added, and they look very fierce when Chinese people pass by, like fierce tigers staring at sheep.

Since the outbreak of the incident, the Japanese have taken advantage of the situation to make profits. Many business restaurants (i.e., brothels) have been established inside and outside the city. Now, Chinese brothels in the industrial area and the north and south markets must be approved by the Japanese before they are allowed to operate. The west bank of Julu River is equipped with electric nets, and two small cannons are erected on the soil slope on the east bank. Honjo Shigeru has ordered the vehicles on the Shenyang-Hai Road to be concentrated in Shenyang and used entirely for transporting troops. Six-foot-tall wooden villages are planted in the area from Hwangutun to Masanjiazi, with the words "Showa Agricultural Company leased land." According to the farmers, passage is prohibited where there are villages. (Can be sent on November 24)

The Common People of the Qing Banner in the Old Capital 62

Declaration Against Puyi's Restoration

Swear to Defend Democratic Politics to the Death

Those Who Go Against the Tide Will Destroy Themselves

Dai Purun, Guan Lunyan, and other representatives of the common people of the Qing banner in Peiping, together with ten million common people of the Qing banner, issued a declaration yesterday, vowing to defend democratic politics to the death and denying that Puyi and his royalist remnants use the name of the Manchu people to implement the imperial system. The original text of the declaration is disclosed as follows:

The Manchu people originated from the Sushen. During the time of Tang Yao and Yu Shun, they had already communicated with China. History records that they have been here for a long time. Compared with the various states of the Spring and Autumn Period, they are like Qin, Chu, Wu, Yue, and Qi, Jin, Yan, and Zhao. This is originally a branch and descendant of the Han people, and there is no distinction to be made. Moreover, the places where they live are all Chinese land and belong to one body, which can further prove this. Since the Middle Ages, the Xianbei and Donghu have appeared in the Yellow River and Yangtze River regions for many years. Although there have been many gaps with the Chinese scholars and officials, it is only because of the emergence of one or two ambitious people as leaders. What does this have to do with the common people of the Qing banner? Moreover, confusion and migration have led to the integration of Manchus and Hans, growing together and mutually reinforcing each other. After thousands of years, their racial blood has become assimilated and indistinguishable. It has been like this for a long time. The Aisin Gioro clan ruled the Eight Banners and came to China, striving to distinguish between Manchus and Hans in order to consolidate the foundation of autocracy and benefit from their mutual hatred. However, considering the reality, those who wielded the power of rule were purely members of the Aisin Gioro clan (that is, the so-called Manchu Qing royal family). The common people of the Qing banner were also ruled and exploited. Examining its origins, the so-called Eight Banners were composed of the Siber Mongols, Bargus, Solons, Ichman Manchus, Nikan Wailans, Yehes, and other tribes, as well as the Han army, Boye, border platforms, post stations, and other people. It is like organizing divisions and brigades and deploying teams. However, the name of the Banner People originated from this. They were given bows and arrows, taught horse riding and archery, and led to the front line, fighting bravely. They ended their lives as soldiers, only receiving dozens of strings of grain. Moreover, they had to abide by the rules of their banner. If they crossed a hundred li, they would be treated as fugitives, causing our people to be trapped to death. It was not only difficult to seek knowledge, but also the inherent spirit of perseverance, martial arts, and courage was worn away. It is truly regrettable. However, those who held high ranks, generous salaries, and titles were all Beizi, Beile, Prince, Duke, and Marquis. Those who inherited official positions were all members of the royal family and relatives. They sat high and mighty, exercising power and influence, living in extravagance, and displaying great arrogance. Eventually, during the Guangxu Restoration, they took a small step towards constitutionalism, but it was destroyed by Empress Dowager Cixi and the royal family. This shows that the princes and ministers of the Qing dynasty were stubborn and ignorant, and their corruption had reached its extreme. As for the Banner Soldiers, they were reduced to servants, suffering from hunger, cold, and disease, with no one to care for them. Pressed by livelihood, how could they have time to improve themselves? As a result, the rich became richer, the poor became poorer, the noble became nobler, and the lowly became lowlier. The gap between the classes was as different as heaven and earth. Having already become poor and miserable Banner Soldiers, they also suffered the discrimination of their own kind. During the Xinhai Revolution, countless people died with grievances. Alas, the common people of the Qing banner were only burdened with empty names and suffered real disasters. How could they complain about the hidden pain in their hearts? After the founding of the Republic of China, the political system became republican. The abdicated emperor was still treated favorably. With faith, righteousness, peace, and the world for all, the people of the Qing banner all entered the door of equality and fraternity and roamed in the realm of civilization and reform. For the past twenty years, there has never been a case of seeking separation from the outside world. This is what all of us common people of the Qing banner sincerely unite and can openly announce to our compatriots across the country without shame. It is also due to thousands of years of marriage and the same language and writing, which have led to assimilation. Alas, it is best to live in peace and avoid danger. If you want to seek more happiness, do not create your own misfortune. The abdicated Puyi and his royal family should all live peacefully, live their civilian lives, and share the happiness of the republic. Unexpectedly, it has recently been heard that they have been seduced by Japanese imperialists and are about to ascend the throne and declare themselves emperor. Such confusion, madness, foolishness, and rebellion will ultimately lead to their own destruction, which is the inevitable result. However, in order to express our fundamental opposition to this, we, the common people of the Qing banner, hereby solemnly declare in all sincerity: Puyi's perverse actions are purely the ambition of the Aisin Gioro royal family and its lackeys, and by no means the public opinion of our ten million Banner People. We swear to defend democratic politics and oppose the restoration of the imperial system. As for their borrowing the name of the Manchu people to claim independence, seceding from China, and willingly betraying the country, it is intolerable by national law. We respectfully request public discernment in tears.

Dai Purun, Guan Lunyan, An Deju, Zheng Chengsi, Ma Junchang, Tang Fushui, Tong Dequan, Jin Yinquan, Shuo Yinchang, Luo Yingjie, Fu Wenxian, Huang Chunren, Gao Enlu, Zhao Liande, Yang Wukui, Xi Shaotang, He Wuxing, De Wenxing, Shuang Yukui, Yu Shixuan, Duo Longa, Akchun, Tang Yin, Guang Fuxiang, Fuyu Tian, Lu Wenxuan, Shu Rong, Xu Wenlin, Na Kuiwu, Bai Kui, together with ten million common people of the Qing banner.

Wuhan Regularly Inspects Japanese Goods 63

Hankou Dispatch: Since Japanese Navy Commander Shiozawa left Hankou, the situation between China and Japan seems to have eased slightly on the surface. However, upon closer inspection, the Japanese side is still actively working together from top to bottom to plot against us. According to a report from a certain party, the Japanese side has decided to launch an attack in Hankou and other ports on the 6th of next month, which is credible when evidenced by the secret burying of landmines in Hankou. As for the people of Wuhan, under the restraint of the authorities, they are still accumulating strength to avoid conflict with the Japanese, and the only method of movement is to boycott Japanese goods. The recent actions of the Japanese residents in Hankou, the process of negotiations with the officialdom, and the progress of the people's inspection of Japanese goods are recorded below.

Japanese Secretly Burying Landmines: The Wuhan Garrison Headquarters issued an order to the Hankou Municipal Government on the 28th, stating that according to the report of Wang Shijie, the director of the Hankou Public Security Bureau, Tan Zuoxiao, the captain of the Second Brigade of the Security Bureau, reported on the 23rd of this month that Li Zhaonan, the chief of the 7th platoon of the temporary soldier sentry of the Overseas Chinese Hotel, reported that at about 4:00 pm on the 21st, two Japanese men, dressed in suits, each carrying a small circular iron box, resembling a landmine, followed two Chinese men and went straight to the wall of the Mitsubishi Yoko company to bury them, and left after a while. It was specifically reported for review. Based on this, we immediately went to investigate and inquired with nearby residents. All residents confirmed that the Japanese men buried iron boxes, but it was still difficult to determine whether they were landmines. During this serious diplomatic period, both the real and the virtual should be prevented. In addition to reporting the investigation situation to the commander of the Third District, who forwarded it for verification, and ordering prevention, we also strictly ordered the sentries in that area to pay special attention, keep a distance, and avoid danger. The above situation should be submitted in writing for verification, and we earnestly request that it be transferred to find a way to prevent and maintain order. Based on this, the reported sections concern the security of Hankou City, and it is urgent to consult with the Japanese Consul to dig out and inspect clearly. If they are dangerous goods, they must be taken back for verification and to ensure safety.

Negotiations on Wages at Taian Yarn Factory: After the Taian Yarn Factory stopped working, the municipal government negotiated with the Japanese Consul several times regarding the issue of paying severance fees to the unemployed workers as required by the contract, but there was no result. On the 28th, the municipal government sent another letter to the Japanese Consul, requesting that the factory be ordered to resolve it quickly. It said that according to the letter from your consulate, the manager of the Taian Yarn Factory replied that the factory's temporary suspension of work was actually due to the anti-Japanese society hindering operations, and it was not a permanent shutdown, nor could it be considered a labor-capital problem. As for the temporary unemployment of workers, we regret this, and the factory cannot bear any responsibility. In response to this, the anti-Japanese movement in Wuhan is the result of the general public's patriotic indignation, and the Taian workers have never heard of it. Moreover, the materials stored by the factory in the Hanyang warehouse can supply a long period of work. Now, the factory is automatically suspending work under the pretext of stockpiling products. Therefore, the factory should bear full responsibility for this shutdown. Moreover, the fact that the factory automatically stopped working has caused the workers to become unemployed for no reason, resulting in a request for six months' severance pay. This labor-capital dispute is a mediation mechanism of the government's responsibility, and we do not want this kind of dispute to be unresolved for a long time, which would lose the affection of labor and capital. Therefore, before the issue of severance pay for unemployed workers in the factory is formally resolved, we will provide them with the convenience of borrowing according to the workers' demands. We firmly believe that the factory will have good relief for the unemployed workers who have promoted the factory's business development through labor in peacetime. We are corresponding to reply to your Consul, and we still hope that the Taian Yarn Factory will be ordered to resolve it quickly.

General Inspection of Japanese Goods to Be Held Immediately: The Wuhan Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has decided to hold a general inspection of Japanese goods in the three towns of Wuhan on December 4th. On the 28th, twelve methods were adopted, and the main points are as follows: (1) The deadline for the general inspection of this association will be the end of the period after the completion of the inspection of the designated area. (2) The scope of work and the number of people assigned for the general inspection of the person: (A) Scope of work, the inspection area shall be based on the police area. (B) Number of people assigned, 48 people in each district, 6 people in each group, and inspections will be carried out separately. (3) Daily inspections are limited to one area. (4) The area to be inspected shall be temporarily designated by the association. (5) The boundary of the area to be inspected shall be secretly sent by the association inspectors to prevent leakage. (6) All inspection groups organized by various trade associations shall conduct the general inspection at the same time as this association, but they must first gather with this association when conducting the inspection to obtain close contact in order to unify command and achieve consistent steps. (November 28)

Hubei Province Implements Disaster Relief by District 64

Part of American Wheat Has Arrived in Hankou

Floodwaters in Wuhan Have Not Receded Completely

Hankou Dispatch: Since the violent Japanese invaded, people across the country have been paying attention to the changes in diplomacy, and they seem to have forgotten the survivors of the disaster. The disaster in Hubei Province is the most serious in the country, with a total of ten million victims in the province. More than 1.5 million people are stranded in Wuhan. At present, the floodwaters in Wuhan have not completely receded. Although the disaster victims have been repeatedly sent away, most of them still have no home to return to. In order to relieve the disaster victims and implement flood control, the authorities decided to implement a work-for-relief method. Today (25th), the first batch of 700 tons of American wheat has been transported by the Dehe Wheel, and another 4,500 tons are on the way and will arrive soon. The authorities then decided to repair the embankments according to the planned plan. All the collapsed embankments of the Xiang River and the Yangtze River were divided into five districts for repair. A labor-for-relief management bureau was established in each district. The bureaus were located in Hankou, Xindi, Jianli, Xiantao, and Qianjiang. The district was divided into sections, and a labor-for-relief office was established in each section, accommodating 5,000 workers, divided into ten regiments, each regiment divided into twenty platoons, and each platoon with twenty-five people. The first district covers the area from Wuxue to Jinkou, requiring about 13,737,000 cubic feet of earth and 45,000 workers. The second district covers the area from Jinkou to Chenglingji, requiring about 14,564,000 cubic feet of earth and 50,000 workers. The third district covers the area from Chenglingji to Tuomao, requiring about 16,331,000 cubic feet of earth and 60,000 workers. The fourth district covers the area from Hankou to Xiantao Town, requiring about 7,366,000 cubic feet of earth and 30,000 workers. The fifth district covers the area from Xiantao Town to Qianjiang and the Jingjiang section, requiring about 8,211,000 cubic feet of earth and 40,000 workers. A total of 225,000 workers are needed. As for the distribution of American wheat, 17,410 tons in the first district, 17,350 tons in the second district, 17,125 tons in the third district, 11,650 tons in the fourth district, and 15,480 tons in the fifth district, totaling 85,020 tons. Hankou is the top grain station, and Wuxue Huangshigang, Jianli, and Xindi are the second grain stations for storage and application. The construction period is set from this month to the end of May next year. This is all about the official embankments. As for the people's embankments, the government will also consider repairing them appropriately. (November 25)
