Murder Case in Dachang 122

Near the Xia Miaogen residence in Xiagiazai, Figure 18, Yanghu Township, Dachang, Baoshan County, a male corpse was found lying prostrate at around 6:00 AM yesterday. The corpse had a shaved head and no hat, and was wearing a dark blue cloth short shirt and trousers, with a floral cloth shirt underneath and a pair of blue cloth single trousers. Bruises were found on the back, and there was fresh blood on the mouth and nose. The left foot was red and swollen, and there were rope marks under the two ribs. The Township Police Chief Yang Xi immediately reported to the Township Head Yang Zhong'anlong to investigate. It was determined that the corpse resembled Chen Guixiang from Chenjiazhai. The younger brother of the deceased, Chen Jinxiang, was immediately notified and confirmed that it was true. According to Chen Jinxiang, his brother Chen Guixiang was 44 years old and worked as a shop assistant in Shanghai. He had returned to his hometown to help Yang Jinfazijiao of Beiyanghu marry his daughter-in-law. He left Yang Jinfa's house at around 9:00 PM after dinner and returned to Chenjiazhai. His family did not see him return home that night and initially thought he was staying at a friend's house. They did not suspect anything else, but unexpectedly he was assassinated. After the incident, Township Head Yang Zhong'an reported to the Baoshan County Government to send personnel to inspect and arrest the perpetrators and bring them to justice.

Japanese Soldiers Beat Chinese Again 123

Shi Liangren Injured

Taken to Hospital for Treatment

At 7:00 PM the other day, Shi Liangren, a plasterer residing at No. 1, Yinhua Lane, Xiaoshadu Road, went out after dinner. While walking near Rentailei Shop on Roberts Road, he was suddenly bumped into by a Japanese sailor. Just as he was about to argue with him, he was beaten with a wooden stick by the Japanese soldier. Shi was unable to resist and fled immediately, but it was too late. He was beaten and seriously injured, spitting blood. The crowd was indignant upon seeing this and immediately called Hua Patrol No. 434 to the scene, but the Japanese sailor had already fled. Shi took himself to Shanghai Hospital for treatment.

Zhuang Chunfu Accuses 124

Ren Zhennan's Fraud Case Opens

Lawyer Ren Zhennan was involved in a case where his wife, Jiang Xingjuan, sued him for obstructing morals and harming her. The criminal case was dropped since both parties unconditionally divorced. The court session was originally scheduled to commence the other day, but it was terminated. However, there was also a case where Zhuang Chunfu accused Ren Zhennan of defrauding him of money. The court session was also scheduled to commence the other day. In the afternoon, Judge Qian Chengjun presided over the session regarding Zhuang Chunfu's accusation. According to Zhuang's wife, Zhuang Li, who filed the case, her husband Zhuang Chunfu could not attend due to a stroke. The official asked how much money they had paid Ren Zhennan in total. She answered, "696 yuan for procedures, 280 yuan for official expenses, 1,000 yuan for settlement fees, and another 3,000 yuan plus a 500-yuan check." (Question) "Where did the 3,000 yuan come from?" (Answer) "She took it out from her cloak." (Question) "Where did you hand it over?" (Answer) "In the office." (Question) "What color was the cloak?" (Answer) "Black." (Question) "What kind of collar?" (Answer) "Leather." (Question) "Was the 3,000 yuan wrapped?" (Answer) "Yes, it was wrapped." (Question) "How many people were there?" (Answer) "My husband and I, Zhuang Jihuai, Qian Yumin, and others." (Question) "How did the check come about?" (Answer) "Qian Yumin borrowed it." (Question) "Did you see Qian Yumin hand it over?" (Answer) "I saw him hand it over to Ren Zhennan." (Question) "Where did you settle the matter?" (Answer) "At the China Hotel, first in room 206, then in room 204." (Question) "Why did you change rooms?" (Answer) "Ren opened it." At this point, the official questioned Qian Yumin, "Regarding the lawsuit between Zhuang Chunfu and Wang Lianxiang, did you introduce Ren Zhennan?" (Answer) "I introduced him to Gu Gongyin, who then introduced him to Ren." (Question) "Did you know about the previous 500 taels?" (Answer) "It was handed over in a room at the China Hotel. There was also 1,000 yuan, also at the China Hotel. The 3,500 yuan was handed over in the office. The first time was with cash, the second time was also with cash, and there was also a 500-yuan check that I lent to Zhuang Chunfu from the Shanghai Bank." (Question) "What was the signature?" (Answer) "My friend Han Dingfeng." (Question) "Where did she take the cash from?" (Answer) "Zhuang Li took it out of her cloak." At this point, the official ordered the clerk to bring Qian Yumin out of the courtroom and asked Zhuang Li, "Is the cloak made of wool or satin?" (Answer) "It is made of black satin." The official then summoned Qian Yumin to the stand and asked, "What material is the cloak made of?" (Answer) "Black soft satin." (Question) "What kind of collar?" (Answer) "Leather collar." (Question) "Was the 1,000 yuan wrapped?" (Answer) "It was wrapped." (Question) "When was the agreement reached at the China Hotel?" (Answer) "February 12." (Question) "Why did you say it was the 9th at the Lawyers' Association?" (Answer) "I didn't know there would be this testimony at the time, so I forgot." (Question) "Since Ren Zhennan took the money, why didn't he issue a receipt or any kind of record?" (Answer) "He refused to issue one." At this point, the official asked Ren Zhennan, "Do you have any animosity with Zhuang Chunfu?" (Answer) "As far as the defendant is concerned, there is no animosity. But Qian Yumin seems to have some animosity." (Question) "Did you take the official expenses?" (Answer) "I did." (Question) "What about the 500 taels and 4,500 yuan?" (Answer) "I didn't." (Question) "According to Qian Yumin's testimony, you cannot say you are innocent." (Answer) "Because Qian Yumin asked to borrow money from me and I didn't have it, he holds a grudge. He introduced the case, and a month later he wanted to borrow 200 yuan." The official asked Qian Yumin, "Did you borrow money from him?" (Answer) "Yes, it was last December. He owed me money from playing cards and didn't pay it back, so I didn't want to ask for it, so I wrote him a letter asking to borrow money." At this point, he asked the prosecutor Yang for his opinion, and the official announced the end of the debate and awaited the verdict.

Chen Xuezhen's Heartbreaking Past 125

Seduced by a Neighbor in Her Youth

Lived Together for Years, Too Boring

Recently Discovered He Has a Wife

Sues for Damage to Family

Chen Xuezhen, a 23-year-old woman from Wuxi residing at No. 172, Weixin Lane, Jiangyuan Lane, Xinzha Road, recently hired lawyer Xiaoxiaoxian to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court accusing Wang Lisanzai of damaging the family and other charges. The defendant, Wang Lizai, did not appear. According to the plaintiff, Chen Xuezhen, in January of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the defendant and I were neighbors. At that time, I was not yet 20 years old, young and ignorant. The defendant took advantage of my mother's absence and used tricks and sweet talk to seduce me into his home. He lied that he worked for the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and earned 50 or 60 yuan per month. If we lived together, he said we could maintain a family life. I was seduced into having sex with him and was instigated to leave my mother and live with him. Later, in the 18th year of the Republic of China, the defendant, under the alias Ye Rongsheng, was sentenced to six months in prison by the local court for committing fraud. At that time, I still visited and provided him with supplies. When he was released from prison, he lied that he would be working at a certain institution soon and asked me to find a way. I also spent a lot of money, a total of 798 yuan, and then he disappeared. I have been living in my mother's house for two years, and I still don't know the defendant's address. I recently learned that the defendant already has a wife. I am extremely angry and have therefore filed a lawsuit, requesting that he be punished according to the law and that he be ordered to compensate for damages of 798 yuan. Judge Feng verified the statement and ordered the case to be adjourned and the defendant summoned for further questioning.

Ten Years of Marriage, Broken in a Day 126

Both Parties Unable to Tolerate Each Other

Divorce is Mediated

Geng Guoxiang, a nurse at the Red Cross Branch on Chihang Bridge, Xinzha Road, and his wife, Zhu Yulian (also a Red Cross staff member), lived together at No. 598, Xinzha Road. The couple's relationship was quite harmonious on weekdays, but recently they suddenly quarreled over trivial matters, which led to the breakdown of their love. Zhu went to the Mediation Office of the First Special District Court to request a divorce. The other day, Judge Li presided over the hearing. According to Zhu Yulian, the reason for requesting a divorce was that Geng beat and abused her from time to time. Geng Guoxiang claimed that there was no abuse of Zhu and that there were two children at home. If they divorced, the children would not be cared for. Therefore, he could not agree with his wife's request. Judge Li persuaded the two parties not to disregard their ten years of marital love over trivial matters and to consider their children, who were their own flesh and blood, and that they should make up as before. However, neither party realized this, and Mr. Li ordered that the mediation failed and that a formal lawsuit should be filed separately.

Maid Wrongly Accused, Commits Suicide in Anger 127

Gu Zonglin, a wealthy merchant, was the president of a major bank in Heilongjiang and possessed great wealth. His wife, Mrs. Xu, lived in the Public Concession, No. 2308, Xiude Lane, Fuxu Road, and had several children. Therefore, she hired five or six male and female servants. One of them was Zhou Kainan, a female servant from Ninghai, 30 years old, who had been in the Gu residence for two years. She was diligent in her work and attentive in her service, so she was deeply favored by the mistress, who encouraged her. Unfortunately, when Shenyang fell and Heilongjiang Province was occupied, Gu's whereabouts were unknown, causing Mrs. Xu great anxiety. The other day, she received a telegram from her husband, informing her that he had safely arrived in Beiping. Mrs. Xu was overjoyed upon hearing this and planned to go to Beiping alone to meet her husband that day. When she was packing her luggage, she intended to take her female servant Zhou Kainan with her so that she could take care of her along the way. However, Zhou had just received a letter from her hometown, reporting that a funeral was urgently needed. She was dismissed, which disappointed the mistress greatly. When the luggage was being transported, a package of clothes suddenly disappeared. The mistress, in a fit of rage, used it as an excuse to accuse Zhou of stealing and sternly rebuked her, and then left by car. Zhou Kainan suffered this injustice and was extremely angry. At around 7:00 PM in the evening, she secretly swallowed raw opium and committed suicide. At 2:00 AM the next day, her companion noticed and urgently called the nearby obstetrician Qi Xiuzhen to come for diagnosis. It was found that the poisoning was serious, and she was immediately sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. She died at 6:00 AM yesterday morning. The body was transferred to the autopsy office to await a report from the court for inspection.

Qian Wangping Runs a Fake Hospital to Swindle Money 128

This summer, a couple from Wenzhou, Qian Wangping and his wife, suddenly rented a flat opposite Daxia Middle School on Jiaozhou Road, Huxi, for eight yuan a month. However, Qian's luggage and utensils were quite simple. Qian then opened a hospital in the house, calling it the Couple's Ophthalmology Hospital, and also treated emergency rescues for poisoning, swallowing gold, and difficult and complicated diseases. However, due to its remote location, business was not very developed, causing several households, such as the neighboring Jingqi Store and the Asia Shoe Store, to be owed more than one hundred yuan by Qian. Recently, Jiang Sanhe, the owner of Jiangtongsheng Bicycle Shop, hired Qian Wangping to treat his eight-year-old son's pinkeye. The fee was agreed upon to be twenty yuan, including medicine. Unexpectedly, after several treatments, not only was it ineffective, but the left eye was blinded. Jiang was eager to save his son and negotiated with Qian, but his right eye was also heavy. Qian claimed that it was due to insufficient medicine and that he needed to purchase medicine from Chinese and Western pharmacies to restore his vision. During the interval, he borrowed a bicycle from Jiang to buy medicine. Jiang was unaware of the trick and generously lent him a new bicycle. However, Qian disappeared. Jiang went to Qian's hospital to inquire and saw that the double doors were closed and there was no sign of anyone. Realizing something was wrong, he immediately inquired with the neighboring shops, who all said that they were owed money. They immediately gathered together and went to the hospital, opened the door, and saw only a camp bed and a few broken tables and chairs. They now plan to hire a lawyer to petition the government to arrest him.

Carrying a Murder Weapon and Robbery 129

Sentenced to Eight Years in Prison

The robber Zhang Chenghua, at 8:00 AM on October 29th, colluded with two other accomplices who were at large and used weapons to rob the Sen Tai Pawnshop at No. 40, Dongxinqiao Street, French Concession (the shop had just opened the door), stealing hundreds of yuan in cash. They escaped northward, and the owner of the pawnshop and his staff followed behind. The two robbers lost track of them. Zhang turned west from Aida Road into Mintini Shade Road, and fled south to the front of the YMCA, where he was apprehended by the owner of the pawnshop and his staff. They took a pistol from Zhang's hand. Nineteen bullets were brought to the police station. It was found that Zhang had robbed the Lantai Pawnshop opened by Guo Liangfu at No. 324, Lanwei Road, on the morning of August 24th, obtaining 236 yuan, which was divided up. He was sent to the Second Special Court Police Station and prosecuted for robbery. Judge Xiong Huihua questioned the defendant several times, and the defendant confessed to the robbery. After the court appointed a lawyer to defend him, it announced the end of the trial and awaited the verdict. Yesterday, when the verdict was due, Judge Xiong arrived at the first criminal court at 3:00 PM and ordered the defendant to be brought to the stand and announced the verdict. Zhang Chenghua was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for each of the two crimes of robbery with weapons by a gang of three or more people, to be executed for eight years. The number of days of detention before the trial was determined to be one day for every two days of imprisonment. The pistol and nineteen bullets were confiscated.

Counterfeit "Old Beauty" Cigars Lawsuit 130

Oriental Tobacco Factory manager Bi Renyingqin, represented by lawyers Yao Zhaomao and Yao Yongli, filed a report with the police, stating that the plaintiff's tobacco factory produces "Old Beauty" cigars in Hong Kong and sells them worldwide. The trademark was registered at the Nanjing Trademark Bureau under number 3076, which was issued in April 1929 and has been published in various newspapers as proof. It has now been discovered that Yongshunyu Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 58-60, Avenue Joffre, is selling counterfeit "Old Beauty" cigars. A request for investigation was made. Upon approval from the court, the police chief issued a search warrant and dispatched detectives to the shop, confiscating more than fourteen boxes of counterfeit cigars, which were taken to the police station. Yesterday, Jiang Bojian, the owner of the shop, was summoned to the First Special District Court for prosecution. The police lawyer Gu Shouxi presented the case, stating that the "Old Beauty" cigars seized from the defendant's shop were identical in style to those of the plaintiff. However, the defendant's cigar boxes bore the words "Little Luzon," constituting a violation of Article 269 of the Criminal Law concerning obstruction of agriculture, industry, and commerce. He requested an investigation. Subsequently, the plaintiff's lawyer presented the situation of the plaintiff's rights. At this point, the lawyer representing the Little Luzon "Old Beauty" Cigar Factory stated that the cigars produced by his client's factory were the genuine "Old Beauty," and that the plaintiff's factory was in fact imitating them. The trademark of his client's factory had been involved in a lawsuit at the Executive Yuan, which has not yet been resolved. Now, the plaintiff intends to bring this case under false pretenses, attempting to obstruct the business of the genuine "Old Beauty." Now that his client's factory has learned of the case, they wish to join the lawsuit and request permission to countersue the plaintiff for the crime of obstruction. The plaintiff's lawyer rose to refute, stating that this case was initiated by his client, and there was no need for the other lawyer to participate. If there were any acts of counterfeiting, a separate lawsuit could be filed. The judge agreed with this point and ordered the lawyer representing the Little Luzon Tobacco Factory to leave. When questioned, Jiang Bojian stated that the "Little Luzon Old Beauty" cigars were purchased from Yongtaixiang Tobacco Shop on Henan Road and that he was unaware of the counterfeiting. He also requested a lawyer for defense and asked for a postponement. The presiding judge ordered Jiang to provide a shop guarantee for his release and granted a postponement for further interrogation.

Male Corpse Strangled at the End of Gonghe Xin Road 131

Near the Tongjia Creek Cemetery behind Xin Yingpan at the end of Gonghe Xin Road, Zhabei, at about 2 PM yesterday, a male corpse was discovered strangled. The deceased was approximately thirty years old, wearing a blue cloth lined jacket, blue cloth pants, white socks, and black shoes. Beside the body was a melon-shaped small hat. There were marks on the deceased's neck from a rope, and blood was flowing from the mouth. The Fourth District Public Security Bureau has reported the case to the court for examination.

Gu Jinbao Dies Tragically 132

Head Caught in Machine Wheel

Instantly Skull Shattered and Bleeding to Death

Gu Jinbao, a native of Wuxi, aged twenty, was delivering food to the Yihe Yarn Factory on Taopeng Road at around 11:45 AM yesterday. He was careless and his head was caught in the machine wheel, instantly shattering his skull and causing profuse bleeding. He was taken to the hospital for treatment by the factory, but died soon after due to the severity of his injuries.

National Goods League 133

At the sixth regular meeting of the National Goods Promotion League Committee, Commissioner Wang Xingyi proposed an emergency motion to promote the wearing of clothing made from domestic silk and cloth. The slogan would be widely publicized to raise awareness. Guanlong Photographic Materials Company Opens Tomorrow 135

Mr. Zhou Dongsui has been in the photographic materials business for a long time. Paris Lady Cigarettes Sell Well in Other Cities 136

Huafa Tobacco Company is a rising star in Shanghai's cigarette industry, producing several brands including "Paris Lady" and "West Beauty." The "Paris Lady" brand, with its exquisite and unparalleled packaging decoration, is particularly rare and eye-catching. Since its launch, it has been highly praised by Chinese people. Manager Liu Yanqing is a renowned overseas Chinese with a reputation as a successful businessman from Fujian. He has an extraordinary business vision and focuses all his efforts on promoting sales in other cities, demonstrating unique ingenuity. There are traces of "Paris Lady" cigarettes all over the country. Business is booming. This is good news for domestic cigarettes.

Public Memorial Service for Wang Caiyun 137

Mr. Wang Caiyun, a native of Fenghua, was the founder of Rongchangxiang on Nanjing Road. He was public-spirited, devoted to society, and the first to establish the Shanghai Business Community Joint Association. Later, he advocated for the civil rights of residents in the concessions and initiated the Taxpaying Chinese Association. He did not dwell on his achievements and was a model for businessmen. When the May Thirtieth Movement occurred, he angrily closed his business and returned to his hometown. He dedicated himself to various local affairs such as road construction, river dredging, bridge building, and price stabilization. He was particularly devoted to founding the Fenghua Orphanage. He came to Shanghai this autumn for business and suddenly fell ill and died. Those who heard the news mourned him. His relatives and friends have scheduled a memorial service for December 1 at the Ningbo Association on Xizha Road to express their grief. It is expected that the event will be a grand and solemn occasion.

Fire at Damatou Street 138

Shunzhichai Gunny Bag Shop at No. 77 Damatou Street in Nanshi carelessly caught fire around 1 AM yesterday. In an instant, fierce flames soared, piercing the roof. Upon learning of the fire, firefighting teams from various districts rushed to connect hoses and fought the blaze for about an hour before it was extinguished. As a result, the rear building of the shop was destroyed. The fire also spread to three adjacent houses of Renyuanyong Straw Mat Shop, which were completely burned down, resulting in significant losses. When the fire was raging, Xu Renshan, the guard police officer from the eleventh post of the patrol station, learned of the fire and rushed to the scene, taking Zhou Jinquan, a shop assistant from the gunny bag shop, and Chen Zixiang, a Ningbo native from the straw mat shop, to the First District Station. After preliminary interrogation by the station chief, due to the fire, he ordered that a document be prepared and submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

The Fourth District Coal Ship Transportation Union yesterday submitted a report to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau stating that it was falsely accused of illegally forcing mergers. They requested swift relief to maintain their lives. The original address of the association was at No. 1537 Wusong Road, but it was moved to the new association hall at No. 822 Hengfeng Lane because it was insufficient for office space. On the 27th of this month, the second landlord, Wu Xiaofa, lost his belongings and went to the Minhang Road police station to make a false accusation, strongly pointing to the association's personnel as the perpetrators. The police station immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to search the union, but nothing was found. The worker Xia Celai was arrested and forced to confess. Upon investigation, it was found that the association's members were all loyal comrades and would not dare to do such illegal things. The worker was immediately released. Upon hearing the news, all the members of the association were extremely indignant and requested that a report be submitted to the court, so as to quickly bring the false accuser to justice in accordance with the law, to protect the people's lives and maintain humanity.

Reader Correspondence

A Message from Mr. Liu Mingsan (Seeking to Awaken the Entire Nation.) 150

The situation is urgent. There is only one way to seek the awakening of the entire nation: (A) The lack of cooperation between the people and the government is the greatest weakness of China. The way to remedy this is through cooperation between officials and civilians, but it should depend on the degree of awareness of the government. (B) Work hard on propaganda among the lower and middle classes (non-intellectuals), explaining how precarious China's national situation is, how dangerous the nation's position is, how important the gains and losses in the eastern provinces are to the other provinces, and how the imperialist powers are invading and oppressing. Find ways to spread this among the people to awaken their awareness. As for newspapers, books, leaflets, slogans, and various special publications, they are particularly useful tools for propaganda and should be widely printed with simple and clear explanations of current events, along with illustrations and posters, and posted in remote villages, factories, wine shops, tea houses, and shops to make them immediately understandable to the people. The power to stimulate the people and influence the masses should be more widespread than written propaganda. (C) Collect various atrocities committed by the Japanese in our Northeast and make glass slides (preferably in color) to be distributed to movie theaters across the country to be shown during movie screenings, shocking the viewers and creating a lasting impression, like the sound of evening drums and morning bells, never to be forgotten. (D) Implement a thorough economic severance plan with Japan. The most important key to whether economic severance with Japan can be achieved depends on the level of awareness of merchants across the country. If merchants do not privately sell Japanese goods, then Japanese goods can be prevented from entering our markets without resistance. As for the Japanese goods that have been sealed up this time, they should absolutely not be sold publicly on the grounds of financial congestion. In the past, the Zheng merchant Xian Gao used twelve oxen to save Zheng state, a story that has been passed down as a good deed for thousands of years. If our merchants have a modicum of conscience, they will certainly be able to catch up and emulate Xian Gao. (Regarding the issue of enemy goods, they should be handled in two categories:) (1) All luxury enemy goods should be disposed of in the same way as opium, by burning them publicly to show our determination. (2) All daily-use enemy goods should be registered and sealed up, and a circulation method should only be considered after the government announces the severance of diplomatic relations. Public sale is absolutely not allowed at present. In addition, what our industrial and commercial sectors should strive to do: (1) is to investigate, to investigate Japanese goods and the factories, banks, shipping companies, shops, and various businesses established by Japanese merchants in our inland areas, as the foundation for resistance. (2) is to promote, to promote domestic goods, to establish factories, to collect and compare domestic products for exhibition, and to strive for excellence to benefit the people and the nation. (3) is to manufacture, to manufacture substitutes for various Japanese goods to avoid the disadvantage of rejecting them but then welcoming them.

Free Talk

The Sound of Anti-Japanese Resistance

— Shou Man

The word "fear" only exists in the dictionary of a slave of a conquered nation.

The five-minute fervor is a common ailment of the Chinese people. But all victories also depend on the effort in the final five minutes.

Inwardly, calmness allows both sides to understand each other and resolve disputes. Outwardly, calmness is sufficient to show weakness and invite foreign aggression.

The anti-Japanese movement must not be like the intermittent fever of malaria, fluctuating between hot and cold. It must be like the flow of rivers, ceaseless day and night.

Bees are the smallest of insects. Anyone who destroys their nests will surely be stung by the swarm. If a nation is destroyed and a family is wiped out and there is no resistance, it is truly worse than being a bee.

Informal Talks from the Not-at-Court Studio

Dialogue Before the God of War (2) 152

"Once the war starts, Japan will certainly use its navy to blockade all of China's treaty ports. I'm afraid that once the economic lifeline is cut off, everything will be over. In my opinion, fighting is more likely to lead to disaster than good fortune."

"If Japan is very stupid, it might do that. I think they have even smarter strategies hidden in their wallets. China's treaty ports, especially Shanghai, are the base for imperialists to carry out economic aggression. Blockading the treaty ports is a general blow to the great powers, especially Britain and the United States. Japan at least wants Britain and the United States to stand on the sidelines now. How can they come up with such a challenging and inferior plan? The strategy that Japan is now adopting is to stir up bigger things to cover up smaller things. You see, he used the Korean massacre to cover up the Wanbaoshan incident, and the invasion of the three northeastern provinces to cover up the Korean massacre, which is the process of this strategy."

"What major event is Japan still hiding to cover up the invasion of the three northeastern provinces?"

"Why do you see that he must cross the Middle East Road to take Qiqihar? To challenge Soviet Russia! If Soviet Russia falls for his plan, Britain and the United States will have to stand on Japan's side. At that time, everyone in the world will only have the war between Japan and Russia in mind, the war between capitalism and communism. Who cares what Japan's invasion of the three northeastern provinces is all about? So, the three northeastern provinces can become a consolation prize for the imperialists to Japan. So, my worry is in Soviet Russia's plot, not in the blockade of the seaports."

"Declaring war now seems like a desperate gamble. You see, it's better to suffer some temporary grievances and wait until ten years of reproduction and ten years of teaching, and then settle accounts with Japan?"

"Ten years of reproduction and ten years of teaching, the Yue state that was defeated in war can adopt this policy. Those who are defeated without war have no qualifications to say this. Since the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895, may I ask how many decades have passed, what has been reproduced, and what has been taught? I boldly say that being defeated without war, and being defeated without fighting, only leads to the reproduction of slaves and the teachings of slaves!"

"I think it's too uncertain to use the fate of the country to gamble like this. We still have to be careful."

"When disaster strikes, righteousness is in front, and even life and death must be seen through, let alone success or failure. The calculations of success or failure are only the tricks of people like Qin Hui and Wu Sangui. Yue Wu Mu, Wen Tianxiang, Shi Kefa, and Ma Zhanshan have only righteousness in their hearts. How can they have ever had a trace of consideration for success or failure!"

The Past of the League of Nations 153

— Lü Bing

When the violent Japanese army invaded and seized the three northeastern provinces, the League of Nations was the organization to uphold justice. As a result, it attracted worldwide attention. Recently, Mr. Wu Chao-chu of our country said, "We should neither overemphasize nor underestimate the League of Nations. After all, the League of Nations is not a supreme government that all participating countries universally respect" (meaning something like that). Mr. Wu once sat on the League of Nations and knows its situation very well. This statement cannot be said to be without its merits. Examining the past achievements of the League of Nations, such as resolving the dispute between Sweden and Finland in 1920, mediating the war between Yugoslavia and Albania in 1921, mediating the dispute between Italy and Greece in 1923, presiding over the British-Turkish boundary demarcation issue in 1925, and resolving the conflict between Bolivia and Paraguay in 1928, it seems that the League of Nations has considerable power in achieving ceasefires and resolving disputes between countries. However, the efforts of the League of Nations in international affairs are not limited to arbitration. According to a report by Mr. Tompkinson, an official of the League of Nations, its successful achievements can be summarized in several aspects. They are specially translated here as a reference for those who want to understand the situation of the League of Nations.

(1) After the end of the European War, the Allied countries captured nearly 500,000 prisoners. They were starving and freezing, with nowhere to settle. The League of Nations decided to send them to Greece, granting them a vast area of 1.2 million acres. At the same time, within Turkish territory, it rescued distressed women and children, reaching a total of 2,000 people.

(2) During the Russian Revolution, there were many massacres and severe epidemics. If they were not contained, Western Europe would also suffer from transmission. The widespread disaster would be like the Black Death that prevailed in Europe during the Middle Ages. The efforts of the League of Nations Health Organization were truly the sole contributor to eliminating this harm.

(3) Labor-capital disputes in various countries around the world are also a point of attention for the League of Nations. Therefore, the League of Nations specially established an International Labor Organization to specifically investigate the labor conditions and living conditions of workers in various countries, as a preparation for resolving various disputes.

(4) In addition, assisting countries in prohibiting the sale of slaves and cracking down on the sale of opium and various drugs are also important duties for the League of Nations itself. It is said that considerable achievements have been made.

The annual membership fees provided to the League of Nations by various countries around the world are about one million pounds. The achievements of the League of Nations are also obvious to everyone. This time, the Japanese army's rampant behavior has been submitted to the League of Nations for discussion. Whether it can be resolved based on public reason is a crucial key to maintaining the credibility of the League today.

The Truth About Japan After Sending Troops to Liaoning and Jilin 154

— Chen Jianwu

This time, the violent Japanese army launched an unprovoked war and occupied our Liaoning and Jilin. Recently, it has also seized our Heilongjiang Province. In the long run, it is the implementation of Giichi Tanaka's memorial to invade Manchuria and Mongolia. In the short term, it is the result of the current Japanese cabinet's Army Minister Minami and Chief of Staff Kanaya, who are both military men. My friend Wan Gengyao studied infantry at the Military Academy and is familiar with the situation in Japan. Yesterday, he spoke to me in detail about the attitude of the Japanese people, both government and public, after Japan invaded and occupied our territory. Sun Tzu said, "Know the enemy and know yourself, and you will not be defeated in a hundred battles." Therefore, I have recorded it below. I think it will also be welcomed by those who are concerned about Sino-Japanese affairs.

Japanese youth feel that the unemployment problem and the economic downturn in their country are becoming increasingly serious. The government cannot solve it. University students and the proletariat generally believe that the only way to reverse the difficult situation is to overthrow the cabinet. Therefore, slogans such as "Kill the Emperor," "Down with the Cabinet," and "Down with the Zaibatsu" are everywhere. In order to maintain his position, Army Minister Minami deliberately created international conflicts to shift the public's attention. The revolutionary trend has temporarily stopped, and the Wakatsuki cabinet can barely survive. After sending troops to Liaoning and Jilin, the Chinese people felt that their territory had been invaded, and the whole country was filled with righteous indignation and hatred of the enemy. Most countries in the world sympathized with us. The Japanese people were well aware of the situation and rose up to give speeches to the military, urging them not to be used by the Army Minister. After this persuasion, many soldiers opposed the war. When Army Minister Minami learned of this, he killed several military officers. The Mitsui zaibatsu, which had previously supported the Minseito, was originally a pro-war element. However, due to the economic severance of relations between China and Japan, their postal ships, coal, cotton yarn, banks, and the Northeast China Soybean Company have successively closed down. The amount of losses is difficult to describe, and there is no hope for future business. Therefore, they urgently made a sharp turn and changed their advocacy of war to advocating peace in order to resolve all disputes as soon as possible. They spoke to the cabinet. Prime Minister Wakatsuki believed that the military was becoming too powerful, and in reality, the Emperor had lost the ability to control the military. He specially invited Elder Prince Saionji to Tokyo to discuss national affairs together. The Seiyukai party members also severely criticized the Minseito's mistakes. In summary, most Japanese, both government and public, sympathize with us in this atrocity. Only a small number of warlords and veterans (according to the Japanese conscription system, these soldiers are those who served in the military during the Tanaka era) are causing trouble. As the saying goes, "Adversity builds a nation." I deeply hope that our compatriots will resist violence, defend against insults, and persevere in economic severance to the end. Then, the island nation of Fusang will have a day when it bows its head and begs for peace.

Magnificent Literature (5) 155

— Tian You

In the past, Liang Rengong (Liang Qichao) fully recorded these twenty-four songs by Gongdu in the "Drinking Ice Studio Poetry Talks," and said:

"The magnificence, liveliness, profundity, and far-reaching nature of its spirit need not be discussed. Even the literary style is unprecedented in two thousand years." I would like to say in one word:

"Whoever reads this poem and does not dance is certainly not a man."

Do we not feel the same way as Ren Gong when we read this poem now?

Gongdu's "Primary School Students' Chorus" has a total of nineteen chapters. In the song, one person sings first, and at the end of each chapter, three people sing together in chorus. Here are the six most magnificent songs:

Listen, you little students, each person has a body and a heaven-given duty. Everything outside the body is your enemy, and everything inside the body is your responsibility. It is better to be unequal to others than to lose ourselves. Relying on parents and leaning on the sky is ultimately useless. Alas! My little students, get rid of the slave mentality and stand tall to be independent.

Listen, you little students, I love my books more than history. This piece of flesh and blood has been passed down from Xuanyuan for more than a hundred generations. The ancestors worked hard, and it is always in our hearts. Alas! My little students, opening the book evokes love for the country, and closing the book brings tears of sorrow for the country.

Listen, you little students, people say that your country has many literary works. That is a sharp pen tip, and this is a little ink stained on silk. What is this crab crawling and wantonly devouring? Strive, strive to compete with each other. Alas! My little students, there is no weak country in the world of literature, and this is not the time to lay down arms.

Listen, you little students, if you want a strong country, first strengthen yourself. Everything outside the dining table is a battlefield, and everything under the shadow of the sword is heaven. Walk together, walk together as if going to face the enemy, singing in the morning and dancing in the evening, wearing black breastplates. Alas! My little students, when alive, be iron men, and when dead, transform into vajras.

Encourage yourselves, you little students, since you are citizens, endure being bandits. Citizens value protecting the qualifications of citizens, and citizens must have the characteristics of citizens. Let the hoe not plant, let the melon seeds divide. The heart is as straight as the black slave's heart. Alas! My little students, burn all the surrender banners, have me and no other country.

Encourage yourselves, you little students, you should fulfill your duties and the meaning of the people. Ying Zheng and Liu Bang have been overthrown many times. The foolish people do not ask about the affairs of the government. You know that the beams are broken and the rafters are collapsing. It is difficult to escape when the sky falls and crushes you. Alas! My little students, vow to exhaust the foolishness of the common people and save the dying sky together.

How can we not dance when we read such wonderful words? (Note 2)

Note 1. For example, Article 3 of the recently promulgated "Educational Outline for Student Volunteer Army" states: "All schools in the country, in terms of curriculum, ... must focus on promoting the national spirit and creating a magnificent and brave atmosphere in courses such as literature and art. All romantic, decadent, and languid literature and art are absolutely prohibited."

Note 2. The "Collected Poems of the Renjinglu Studio" was printed in Japan and is not easy to obtain now. The "Commentary on the Poems of the Renjinglu Studio" is still easy to buy in the market, but the selection is limited.

(End)

Rotary Club of Novels

A Country Bumpkin Arrives in Shanghai Again (32) 156

— Bao Tianxiao

After the country bumpkin finished his meal, he walked out of the Mei Garden Restaurant. He thought to himself, "Now I can go to Meilanfang to find my nephew A Mulian. Should I take a rickshaw or a tram? I've been on the tram for half a day, and it took me across the Grand Theater without reaching my destination. It seems much easier to quickly call a rickshaw and tell him to pull me to Meilanfang."

As he thought, he was looking at the Shanghai night scene. It was about eight o'clock at night, when Shanghai people were having dinner. Chinese and Western restaurants were filled with customers like a tide. The electric lights shone as if every shop had an electric light archway in front of its door. The prostitutes who came out to sing were dressed in gorgeous clothes and sat in shiny rickshaws. The rickshaw pullers, pushing and pulling, ran faster than horse-drawn carriages.

The country bumpkin remembered something. A young man from his village named A Jinlong came to Shanghai to pull rickshaws for a mansion. The master in that mansion was a big guy, and the rickshaw pullers didn't like him. But he insisted on having the rickshaw puller run fast. The old rickshaw pullers shook their heads when they saw him. They said, "Rather than pull this big guy, it's better to carry a coffin." A Jinlong, however, was young and strong. He pulled this master and moved as fast as flying. So the master chose him.

Many people who were jealous of A Jinlong called him a "two-legged horse." The meaning of "two-legged horse" was also a bit malicious. The horse that pulls the cart originally has four legs. Now humans are also doing the work of horses. Horses are livestock and serve humans. They cannot speak and cannot complain to humans. Since they are humans, why should one person sit comfortably in the cart, while the other person runs, panting and sweating, pulling the cart? Humans are also doing the work of livestock, but they are still two legs shorter than livestock. Therefore, the humans who pull the cart got this elegant name, called "two-legged horses."

But the country bumpkin saw the rickshaws pushing and pulling and showing off, and the rickshaw puller was still complacent. He thought to himself that it was clearly four legs running there, but one animal had been replaced by two humans.

"Gee! There are so many female Zhuge Liangs in Shanghai." As he walked, he muttered to himself, saying silly things.

It turned out that when they were putting on a makeshift opera stage in the spring, he had seen a performance of the "Empty City Stratagem." He knew that the name of the person holding a feather fan was Zhuge Liang. He didn't expect that when he came to Shanghai and took a look, every girl sitting in a rickshaw was holding a feather fan. So he sighed and said that there were too many female Zhuge Liangs in Shanghai.

Finance 157

The Bid-Up Gold Market Was Complex Last Week

Fluctuations Occurred Several Times, Resulting in a Gradual Increase. The fluctuations in the bid-up gold market last week were still considerable, the situation was complex, and it seemed to be in a swirling pattern. The turbulent waves were difficult to suppress, with differences of more than ten to twenty taels per day. People's hearts were extremely disturbed and it was difficult to take measures. However, in the end, it gradually increased. From the beginning of the week, it slightly weakened to a minimum of 654 taels, and then the overseas silver market showed different trends. The UK rose and the US shrank, but the exchange rate of Shanghai bills still deviated in the opposite direction. The UK was loose and the US was tight, mainly because the exchange rates between the UK and the US frequently fell. The pound sterling first lengthened by four levels, and the US dollar shrank by 0.25. The domestic market was also the same. Gold companies sometimes bought and sometimes sold, but the spread was opened wider, causing the gold price to break through the 80-tael mark. On Thursday, a new high price of 685 taels was discovered. Later, due to the situation, the news of the Japanese army's advance on Jinzhou and the disruption of Tianjin worsened, and people's hearts were panicked, breaking through the 60-tael mark again. As a result, it was on the border of 70 taels. There were 31 taels of retrospect in these six days. The total continued to rise by 10 taels and 8 qian. The price was settled according to the US dollar. At first, it was pressed around 70 taels, and then it even reached more than 112 taels. The Dalian gang slightly occupied the majority of long positions. As for the Guangdong gang, which was originally short, it engaged in more than 5,000 counterattacks by the end of the week. However, the spot red tape was loose, mainly because the silver market was still tight. The situation in the north was unstable, so the price only increased by 5 taels in the spot bid. In the future, there may still be drastic changes. The general situation of the past week is summarized below.

Different Mentalities Caused Chaos. From Monday (November 23), the silver market was long 1875, the US silver market shrank 125, the pound sterling did not change, and the internal market was tightening. Foreign firms George Joseph and the gold gang were all buying. The gold price initially opened slightly lower by 0.25, at 654.5 taels, followed by 54 taels. Due to the shaking of the Japanese cabinet, the buyers were active, and George Joseph captured short positions, soaring by more than 10 taels to 68 taels. Then, due to rumors that Japan banned the transportation of cash, it plummeted by more than 10 taels, and the afternoon closed at 55 taels and 2 qian. In the afternoon, the market opened at 56.5 taels, followed by 5 taels and 8 qian. Afterwards, Wu and others pursued, and it was heard that a telegram came from Mumbai to buy pound sterling, which boosted people's hearts and broke through 70 taels, reaching 79.5 taels. By the time the market closed, it was 77.5 taels, an increase of 19 taels compared to the previous Saturday. There were 25.5 taels of ups and downs throughout the day. On Tuesday, the silver market was short 1875 for the near term, and did not change for the far term. The US silver price shrank 875, the pound sterling did not change, and the US dollar shrank 75, which also means that the exchange rate shrank. The domestic market seemed to be covering the bid-up gold market. The market opened at 74.5 taels, and then there were ups and downs of more than 10 taels, with considerable fluctuations. Then, a large trader bought in at 79 taels. At noon, Wu and others sold out, only accounting for 67 taels. At noon, it was from 70 taels to 68 taels and 9 qian. In the afternoon, it opened at 71.5 taels, followed by 68 taels to 73 taels and 9 qian. A large trader sold 65.5 taels, and by the time the market closed, it was 70 taels and 08 qian, a decrease of 6 taels and 7 qian compared to the previous day. There were 13.5 taels of ups and downs in total. On Wednesday, the silver market rose by 375, the silver price rose by 375, the pound sterling lengthened by another level, the internal market also lengthened, and the industry sold out, because the exchange rate returned, and the US dollar trend became harder, so the spread was slightly closer. As for the gold price, it immediately dropped by 5 taels and 3 qian when the market opened, to 665 taels and 5 qian, and then only accounted for 57 taels. At noon, there were more buyers, so it became 63 taels and 7 qian, and the market closed at 60 taels and 7 qian. In the afternoon, it opened at 62 taels, and retail traders sold out, to 59 taels. Again, as Mumbai was decreasing, there were still more buyers, rising to 65 taels and 3 qian. By the time the market closed, it was 64 taels and 6 qian, but it was 6 taels and 2 qian less than the previous day. The front and rear markets were up and down 8 taels and 7 qian, the situation was still flat, and the foreign exchange market was closed on Wednesday afternoon. On Thursday, the silver market shrank by 0.25, the US silver market decreased by 375, the pound sterling also shrank by one level, the internal UK was flat and the US was tight, which also meant that the exchange rate shrank again. The bid-up gold market immediately rose by 9 taels and 9 qian, accounting for 724.5 taels. It was also rumored that South Africa maintained the gold standard, and people's hearts were upward, rising to 84 taels. Later, a large trader sold to 73 taels, and the noon closing was 77 taels and 8 qian. In the afternoon, 79.5 taels once reached a new high price of 85 taels, because Wu and other large traders bought hard. Afterwards, the exchange market became easier, and Mumbai suddenly added 13 annas, plummeting by more than 16 taels, to 68 taels and 5 qian. In a moment, Mumbai reported 7 annas smaller, and the price re-emerged to 70 taels, accounting for 74.5 taels. By the time the market closed, it was 72 taels and 7 qian, a decrease of 7 taels and 1 qian compared to the previous day. There were 16.5 taels of ups and downs throughout the day. On Friday, the silver market lengthened 0.25, the US silver market was not in the middle, the pound sterling lengthened by one level, but the US dollar did not change, because there was no exchange market. As for the domestic market, it was wide, and the industry sold out the most. The bid-up gold market opened at 73.5 taels, adding 1 tael and 8 qian, which also meant that the silver market was short, followed by 75 taels. Afterwards, it gradually decreased, but there were 10 taels of ups and downs. The noon closing was 65 taels and 3 qian, and in the afternoon it was 57 taels and 5 qian. The Dalian gang first sold out, followed by 54 taels and 5 qian. Mumbai reported that it was also big. After entering, the buying was strong, accounting for 63 taels and 7 qian. By the time the market closed, it was 62 taels and 8 qian, a decrease of 8 taels compared to the previous day. There were 20.5 taels of ups and downs in one day. On Saturday, the silver market rose again by 5625, the silver price shrank by 125, the pound sterling lengthened by 75, and the US dollar only added 75 due to the exchange rate shrinking again. The domestic market was very different, the UK was loose and the US was tight, and there were not many transactions. Afterwards, it gradually rose, breaking through 70 taels, which also meant that the Guangdong gang's Hengxing was strongly filling the short positions, accounting for 74 taels. Securities 160

Last Week's Bond Prices Continued to Fall Sharply

Falling about Three or Four Yuan More Than the Previous Week

Settlement Was Handled for Only Three Days Throughout the Week

Although the January Futures Market Opened, There Were No Transactions

Last week (from November 23rd to 28th), the bond market situation at the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange was such that, coinciding with the end-of-month futures settlement period, except for the first two days and the last day of the week, the remaining three days were closed for settlement of November futures. Spot transactions were mainly small-scale, with a total turnover of only 41,000 yuan for the entire week. Among them, compilation and dismissal of troops bonds accounted for 9,000 yuan each at 20 customs, consolidation and troop reduction bonds, and 19 customs salt tax bonds each accounted for 5,000 yuan, and the remainder were very small. The price fluctuations in the futures market were very sharp in the first two days of the week, with active trading. On Monday, it totaled more than 15.4 million yuan, and on Tuesday, it also totaled 12.5 million yuan. On the last day of the week, although the 20-year January futures market opened, there were no transactions. The December futures were also maintained due to the bond market, prohibiting new sales, and with only one session in the afternoon, the turnover was only more than 1.4 million yuan. However, due to the Ministry's order prohibiting over-the-counter transactions, the over-the-counter transactions among brokers that were transferred to the account of the exchange on that day amounted to 9,485,000 yuan, with a cumulative total of 38.85 million yuan. Among them, consolidated salt bonds were the most, with consolidated tax bonds at 2.29 million yuan for November futures and 4.34 million yuan for December futures; salt tax bonds at 1.84 million yuan for November futures and 4.12 million yuan for December futures; 20 customs bonds at 1.74 million yuan for November futures and 3.29 million yuan for December futures; 20 customs bonds (rolled) at 1.875 million yuan for November futures and 2.68 million yuan for December futures; 19 good customs bonds at 1.3 million yuan for November futures and 2.655 million yuan for December futures; 19 customs bonds at 1.725 million yuan for November futures and 1.745 million yuan for December futures; troop reduction bonds at 660,000 yuan for November futures and 3.035 million yuan for December futures; compilation and dismissal of troops bonds at 1.425 million yuan for November futures and 2.03 million yuan for December futures; 96 public bonds at 930,000 yuan for November futures and 200,500 yuan for December futures; consolidation six percent bonds at 445,000 yuan for November futures and 190,000 yuan for December futures. However, only the November futures for customs duties opened at 320,000 yuan, and there was no market for December futures. As for the changes in the market prices of various bonds during the past week, the prospect of diplomatic relations with Japan was bleak, and the situation was extremely serious. The League of Nations was also timid and hesitant, and there was no progress in mediation and negotiation. The market sentiment became increasingly weak. Although the bond prices fluctuated greatly on Monday, there were both rises and falls, and the trend was still relatively calm. However, on Tuesday, the market demand was weak, and those who were unable to take delivery of goods urgently sought to sell, causing prices to fall sharply across the board, with declines ranging from two to four yuan. The fall in market prices was almost a new record. However, the impact on the financial market and investment was extremely significant. The Ministry of Finance, in view of this situation, had no choice but to find ways to provide relief, ordering the exchange to comply. The method was to take the closing price on November 24th, that is, last Tuesday, as the standard market price, and the market transaction price could not be lower, and illegal over-the-counter transactions were prohibited. In addition to complying with the Ministry's order, the exchange also suspended new sales transactions in order to maintain the market, while not restricting buyers, in order to alleviate the market. As a result, on the last day of the week, market sentiment stabilized slightly, and market prices rose by about one yuan due to demand exceeding supply. However, as a result, compared with the previous week, they still fell by about three or four yuan. Looking at the future of the securities market, with the exchange absolutely limiting new sales, bond prices are indeed unlikely to continue to fall. However, it is said that the exchange's regulations are temporary measures. If there is a turnaround in the external situation, prices may quickly rebound. Social News

Stories About Tobacco By Fu Lan 165

George Arents of the United States can be regarded as the world's only collector of tobacco books. Books, pamphlets, and ancient judgments are all available, worth a lot of money. Therefore, he specially uses an old iron box to hide those rare versions and copies, with twelve different secret locks added.

He started collecting in 1892, when he was only seventeen years old. One of his uncles was a tobacco grower, so he made this suggestion to him. At present, he is preparing to print a story about tobacco, divided into three volumes, each as thick as a telephone directory, containing many interesting facts, such as Vespucci, who was the first person to mention tobacco in books, in 1505, he saw the Indians of Venezuela grinding tobacco leaves into powder, kneading them into pills, and swallowing them. When they were sitting in canoes and setting off on expeditions, they thought that this could prevent hunger.

The first person to mention smoking in a book was the Spaniard Oviedo, around 1535. He saw the Indians of Haiti burning tobacco and putting it into reed pipes to inhale into their nostrils. As soon as they lit the fire, they immediately sucked frantically. In today's human beings, it will lead to death.

Twelve years later, Oviedo saw some Indians placing dried tobacco leaves on palm leaves, burning them, and inhaling the poisonous gas they emitted. This could make the smoker intoxicated all day long, but no one at the time warned them.

Spenser was the first British writer to mention tobacco. Shakespeare's collection never mentioned tobacco. Arents speculated that this was proof that Shakespeare opposed Bacon, because Bacon mentioned this thing from time to time. Perhaps this great poet, in order to support King James' opposition to smoking, taxed tobacco to 4,000 percent in order to dissuade the people from smoking, so he deliberately avoided mentioning it in his collection of poems.

In the 18th century, there were almost no smokers in England. In the 17th century, smoking was popular throughout England, and all classes competed to smoke as a fashion.

Since snuff rose, smokers gradually decreased, but in the 19th century, smokers revived. In 1864, machines began to be used to make cigarettes, and cigarette rolling machines were invented in 1883, and so on until today.

Tobacco, in general, is considered to be able to treat nasal mucus membranes, cramps, and other diseases. According to Arents' research, during the American Civil War, soldiers applied tobacco under their armpits when they set off to relieve pain.

Arents also found that the world's ancient and modern champion smoker was the Dutchman M.V. Klaes. He died in 1871 at the age of ninety-eight. He smoked about four tons of tobacco in his lifetime. When he was dying, he invited all his smoking comrades and asked them to participate in his funeral together. When the funeral was held, everyone had to smoke, without interruption. At that time, hundreds of comrades came, each given two pipes and ten pounds of tobacco. This funeral was an unprecedented grand event. For a time, the smoke was misty, and people could not be identified on the opposite side.

Wallace Invited to Hollywood By Fu Lan 166

Edgar Wallace, the world-renowned British writer, has recently signed a contract with Sneraud, the general manager of an American sound film company, to write a novel for the company. After years of negotiation by many American film companies, they wanted to obtain his creative services, but without results. This time, the company actually achieved its goal, which is really commendable.

The genius of this writer has long been admired by American filmmakers. They continued their efforts to lure him from England to the United States, but finally failed. This time Sneraud's success is also the triumph of the American sound film industry.

This outstanding British writer, among his contemporary world writers, can be regarded as a number of members. He has written hundreds of novels and countless short stories, and has been diligently engaged in this for the past thirty years. In England, he securely sits in a chair among two or three outstanding modern writers.

His books sell millions of copies in the United States every year. His works have been translated into various countries. Mysterious and adventurous stories are especially his forte. In addition to short and long novels, he has also written many scripts, some of which have been performed on Broadway in New York and have been very successful. For example, the play "On the Spot" produced by 勗弁德 Company was performed at the 福來斯德 Theater and is an example.

American theaters first performed his works in 1913. At that time, he had already become a successful novelist. He wrote a script entitled "Manager's Dream," which did not attract attention. So he changed to writing musical comedies, such as "Hello, Everyone," "Are You There," "Smile," "Soldier," "Dihuangniu," and so on.

In 1926, he began writing musical scripts and was listed as the vanguard of a group of London playwrights. First came a "Complete Gentleman," followed by "Terror," "The Man Who Changed His Name," "Flying Squad," "The Howler," "The Unknown," and "Calendar," and so on.

Wallace's signing of the contract is only the beginning of the first step of work on Sneraud's side. They are preparing to set up a method to attract general famous writers to write a valuable original work for the sound film company.

Book Reviews

An Overview of Local Autonomy · Dawn · Light 167

By Lin Zhongke

Mr. Sun Yat-sen said in the "Fundamentals of National Reconstruction," "During the period of political tutelage, the government should send personnel who have been trained and passed examinations to various counties to assist the people in preparing for self-government..." and also said, "Build local autonomy, promote the development of civil rights." We all know that the Party's revolutionary policy is divided into three stages: military government, political tutelage, and constitutional government. The foundation of constitutional government is laid on political tutelage, and the work of political tutelage is included in local autonomy. It can be seen that the cause of local autonomy is the fundamental work of our Party's unique spirit. In other words, the idea of local autonomy has clearly shifted from a textual program to a political program today. Therefore, at the beginning of this political tutelage, when local autonomy is being carried out, it is not meddlesome for me to introduce this book.

The author of this book, Mr. Lin Zhongke, is a scholar with rich writings. He has had the ideal of realizing local autonomy in his mind for more than ten years. This book is the accumulation of the author's blood and sweat in researching local autonomy for more than ten years.

The book is divided into six chapters. The first chapter is an introduction, the second chapter is the composition of local groups, the third chapter is the organs of local groups, the fourth chapter is the division of local autonomy, the fifth chapter is the application of local autonomy, and the sixth chapter is the supervision of local autonomy. The following is a brief analysis of each chapter:

Chapter 1, Introduction. This chapter explains "the basic concepts of local autonomy." In the middle, the meaning of local autonomy and the mission undertaken by those who handle autonomy are explained in detail.

Chapter 2, Composition of Local Groups. This chapter is divided into three sections. The first section is "the area of local groups," the second section is "the residents of local groups," and the third section is "the citizens of local groups." In the first section, it is divided into the first paragraph, "the nature of the area of local groups," which provides a very detailed explanation of the nature and facilities of the area. The second paragraph, "the changes in the area of local groups," stipulates by law how to change its area scope, and various situations such as the disposal, division, merger, and boundary changes of districts, townships, and towns within the area. The second section is "the residents of local groups." This section explains what constitutes a resident of a local group, and the various corresponding conditions stipulated by law for residents of local groups. The third section is "the citizens of local groups." The first paragraph includes "the meaning and origin of citizens," and the second paragraph is "the requirements of citizens." Here, the author believes that citizens should have both active and passive requirements to be called citizens. The third paragraph talks about "the rights of citizens," which are the four political powers of election, recall, initiative, and referendum. Based on the Party's position, and referring to various systems in various countries around the world, the author elaborates on the origin and how to use the four political powers. Taking the referendum power alone, the author divides it into six categories in form: (1) mandatory referendum power, (2) arbitrary referendum power, (3) ordinary referendum power, (4) advisory referendum power, (5) consultative referendum power, and (6) approval referendum power.

Moreover, each referendum power has its own special function. The other three political powers are divided and explained as precisely as the referendum power. For readers, this is very clear and does not require much thought.

Chapter 3, Organs of Local Groups. This chapter is divided into two sections. The first section, "the will organ of local groups," such as the county assembly for the local autonomous body of a county, details the nature, organization, powers, and deliberation methods of the county assembly. The second section, "the administrative organ of local groups," such as the county government, clearly explains how the county magistrate should be elected, and what powers the elected county magistrate should have.

Chapter 4, Division of Local Autonomy. The first sentence of Mr. Sun Yat-sen's handwritten "Law on the Commencement of Local Autonomy" states, "The scope of local autonomy should be a county as a sufficient area. If a county is not possible, then the combination of several villages with fields of twenty or thirty li in length and width can also be used as a pilot area." From this, it can be seen that Mr. Sun Yat-sen also advocated the division of local autonomy. This chapter is divided into three sections. The first section is "district autonomy," which includes "regarding district people's congress," "district office," "district supervision committee," "district mediation committee," "district finance," etc., all of which have thorough and clear regulations. The second section is "township autonomy," in which the administrative scope is entirely in accordance with legal regulations. The third section is "neighborhood autonomy," whose organization and affairs are simpler than those of districts and townships. Although the scope of neighborhoods is small, the author has not neglected its systematic description due to the narrowness of the scope.

Chapter 5, Application of Local Autonomy. At the beginning of this chapter, the author says, "The application of local autonomy means how local autonomous bodies manage their own functions and how they carry out activities in society." Now that political tutelage has begun, and local autonomy is being carried out throughout the country, a basic practical issue regarding "the application of local autonomy" can in no way be neglected. Therefore, the author of this book has listed many actual situations in society in a concrete way as citations for each section of this chapter.

This chapter is divided into three sections. The first section is "Basic Concepts of Autonomy." This section is explained from two points: one is "the foundation of autonomy," and the other is "inherent affairs and delegated affairs." The foundation of autonomy is the autonomous ability recognized by the national legal system. Here, the author explains in detail the meaning and function of the five powers of government, and describes the comparison between the autonomy of various European countries and the autonomy of our country.

The second section is "the Administrative Management Power of Local Groups," which is divided into "the meaning of the right to organize," "the content of the organization," "the right to formulate laws and regulations," "the content of the right to formulate autonomous laws and regulations," "the process of formulating regulations," "the limits of public labor management," "the application of the right to public labor management," and "coercive power," explaining one by one how local areas should set up and how they should reform or abolish affairs. Those who care about social problems can get many concrete remedies and facility policies here, which is of great help to those currently engaged in the labor movement.

The third section is "the Financial Management Power of Local Groups," regarding "property management rights," "expenditure financial rights," "expenditure of local autonomous bodies," "local taxes," and "public burden," the author, based on public finance, gives a very full explanation of how local autonomous bodies should manage the above items.

Chapter 6, Supervision of Local Autonomy. Before we can understand what the supervision of local autonomy is, we naturally need to know what supervision is first. Fortunately, regarding this urgent question to be answered, the author has clearly answered it for us in the book: "The meaning of supervision should be divided into two points: one is supervision in the relationship of public law, and the other is supervision in the relationship of private law. The former is like the 'legislative supervision,' 'judicial supervision,' and 'administrative supervision' of various countries, and the latter is like the supervision of an agent over a sub-agent, the supervision of an employer over an employee, and the supervision of a person with parental authority over an incapable person."

This chapter is divided into two sections. The first section is "Basic Concepts of Autonomous Supervision." This section is divided into three key points: one is "the necessity of autonomous supervision," two is "the form of autonomous supervision," and three is "the organs of autonomous supervision." The second section is "the content of the supervisory power," which includes nine items: the power of monitoring, the power to cancel orders and dispositions, the power of substitute resolution, the power of special resolution and disposition, the power of substitute execution, the power of dissolution, the power of disciplinary action, the power of approval, and the reservation of decision power. The above powers all have their own meanings and tasks. Although the names are different, they are all mutually conditional and mutually related. After the establishment of public offices such as districts and townships, autonomous supervision will perform its duties to seek lasting welfare for the local groups concerned.

Summarizing the above chapters, I believe that this book is the most comprehensive and substantial book on local autonomy. In fact, there is a pitiful lack of books on relatively perfect local autonomy in China today. The author has created this voluminous work of more than 100,000 words as a result of more than ten years of painstaking research. It is truly a brilliant flower blooming in academic circles, and it is undeniable that it serves as a guiding light for those who handle local autonomy. The period of political tutelage has unfolded before our eyes. In order to promote the early realization of the work of local autonomy, I am happy to introduce this book to readers. I sincerely pray that this voluminous work with rich materials will achieve great results in the shortest possible time.

Book Review Guidelines 168

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc., books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new artists at home and abroad and illustrations related to the text.
